[줄 664] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - This chapter identifies the various means of transferring a ship from the land on which it is constructed to the water.
[줄 665] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - The traditional end launching process is described as this is the most complex method.
[줄 666] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - End launching is now less common as most newer shipyards have a building dock.
[줄 667] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Other methods are less common and include side launching, a ship lift, a floating dock, or a pontoon.
[줄 668] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - Whilst many modern shipyards now construct ships in building docks and float them out and some utilize ship lifts, a good number of long-established shipyards are still launching ships in the traditional manner.
[줄 669] [100.0%] (36/36) ✅ 유지 - A significant advance has been provided by computer programs that allow prior assessment of the performance of the ship and the loading it may experience during the launch, both on the ways and in the water.
[줄 670] [100.0%] (36/36) ✅ 유지 - Launching involves the transference of the weight of the ship from the keel blocks, shores, etc on which it was supported during construction, to a cradle on which it is allowed to slide into the water.
[줄 671] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Normally the vessel is launched end on, stern first, but a number of shipyards located on rivers or other narrow channels are obliged to launch the vessel sideways.
[줄 672] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - Vessels have been launched bow first, but this was a rare occurrence as the buoyancy and weight moments, as well as the braking force, are generally more favorable when the vessel is launched stern first.
[줄 673] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - There is also a danger of damage to propellers and rudders as the ship leaves the end of the slipway.
[줄 674] [100.0%] (3/3) ✅ 유지 - All rights reserved.
[줄 675] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - End launches On release of a holding mechanism the launching cradle with the ship slides down the ground ways under the action of gravity.
[줄 676] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - When the stern has entered the water the vessel is partly supported by buoyancy and partly by the ground ways.
[줄 677] [100.0%] (41/41) ✅ 유지 - If this buoyancy is inadequate after the center of gravity of the ship has passed the way ends, the ship may tip about the way ends, causing large pressures on the bottom shell and on the ends of the ground ways.
[줄 678] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - To avoid this the greatest depth of water over the way ends should be utilized, and the ground ways extended into the water if necessary.
[줄 679] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Where this proves impossible it becomes necessary to strengthen the way ends and provide shoring in the bottom shell region, which is likely to be damaged.
[줄 680] [100.0%] (5/5) ✅ 유지 - These remedies are often expensive.
[줄 681] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - As the vessel travels further into the water the buoyancy becomes sufficient to lift the stern.
[줄 682] [94.1%] (16/17) ✅ 유지 - The vessel then pivots about the forward poppets, i.e the fore end of the launching cradle.
[줄 683] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - These are designed to take the load thrown on them by the pivoting action, the load being widely distributed in order not to squeeze out the lubricant between the sliding surfaces.
[줄 684] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Shoring may also be found necessary forward in the ship to prevent structural damage at the time the stern lifts.
[줄 685] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Building slipway Conventional slipways or berths are relatively solid and reinforced with piles to allow them to sustain the weights of ships built upon them.
[줄 686] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - During building the keel blocks take the greater part of the weight, the remainder being carried by shores and, where used, bilge blocks.
[줄 687] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Foundations under the probable positions of ground ways should also be substantial, since during a launch the ways are subject to large pressures.
[줄 688] [85.7%] (30/35) ✅ 유지 - Keel blocks are arranged so that the height of keel above the ground is 1.25– 1.5 m, giving reasonable access, but not too high so that a large amount of packing is required.
[줄 689] [97.1%] (33/34) ✅ 유지 - At the bow the height of the keel must be sufficient to allow the ship's forefoot to dip the required amount without striking the ground during pivoting when the stern lifts at launch.
[줄 690] [93.9%] (31/33) ✅ 유지 - To suit the declivity of the launching ways determined beforehand, the keel is also inclined to the horizontal at about 1 in 20, or more where the shipyard berths have a larger slope.
[줄 691] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - To transfer the ship from the building blocks to the launching cradle, the commonest practice is to drive wedges into the launching cradle.
[줄 692] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - This lifts the ship and permits the removal of the keel and bilge blocks together with the shores.
[줄 693] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - In large ships it becomes necessary to split the blocks to remove them, but several types of collapsible blocks have been used to overcome this difficulty.
[줄 694] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - One type is the sand box, which contains sand to a depth of 80–100 mm held in a steel frame located between two of the wooden blocks.
[줄 695] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - This steel frame may be removed and the sand allowed to run out.
[줄 696] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Another type is a wooden block sawn diagonally, the two halves being bolted so that they collapse on removal of the bolts.
[줄 697] [91.7%] (22/24) ✅ 유지 - REINFORCED BERTH Bilge blocks Shore Space for launching ways Keel blocks Shore Concrete Space for launching ways Bilge blocks Figure 15.1 Building blocks.
[줄 698] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Launching ways and cradle The fixed ground ways or standing ways on which the cradle and ship slide may be straight or have a fore and aft camber.
[줄 699] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - Transversely the ground ways are normally laid straight but can be canted inwards to suit the ship's rise of floor.
[줄 700] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - Usually, the ground ways have a small uniform fore and aft camber, say 1 in 400, the ways being the arc of a circle of large radius.
[줄 701] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - This means that the lower part of the ways has a greater declivity than the upper part of the ways.
[줄 702] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - As a result a greater buoyancy for the same travel of the ship beyond the way ends is obtained, which will reduce the way end pressures.
[줄 703] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Additional advantages are increased water resistance slowing the vessel and a bow height that is not excessive.
[줄 704] [100.0%] (41/41) ✅ 유지 - The slope of ground ways must be adequate to allow the vessel to start sliding and, if too steep, a large amount of shoring will be required to support the bow; also, the loads on the releasing arrangements will be high.
[줄 705] [75.0%] (12/16) ✅ 유지 - Straight sliding ways have declivities of the order of 1 in 25 to 1 in 16.
[줄 706] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Generally two ground ways are fitted, the distance between the ways being about one-third the beam of the ship.
[줄 707] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - It is often desirable that the cradle should be fitted in way of longitudinal structural members and the ground ways over slipway piling, these considerations deciding the exact spacing.
[줄 708] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Some large ships have been launched on as many as four ways, and in Germany and the Netherlands it is common practice to launch vessels on a single center-line ground way.
[줄 709] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - The width of the ways should be such that the launching weight of the ship does not produce pressures exceeding about 20 tonnes per square meter.
[줄 710] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - Ground ways are laid on supporting blocks and extend down to the low water mark so that they are covered by at least 1 meter of water at high tide.
[줄 711] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - To guide the sliding ways as they move over the ground ways, a ribband may be fitted to the outer edge of the ground ways.
[줄 712] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - This could be fitted to the inner edge of the sliding ways, but when fitted to the ground ways has the advantage that it aids retention of the lubricating grease.
[줄 713] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Finally, the ground ways are shored transversely to prevent sideways movement and longitudinally to prevent them from moving down with the ship.
[줄 714] [95.7%] (44/46) ✅ 유지 - The sliding ways, covering about 80% of the length of the vessel, form the lower part of the cradle, the upper part consisting of packing, wedges, and baulks of timber with some packing fitted neatly to the line of the hull in way of the framing.
[줄 715] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - In very fine-lined vessels the forward end of the cradle, referred to as the forward poppet, will need to be relatively high, and may be built up of vertical timber props tied together by stringers or ribbands.
[줄 716] [88.0%] (22/25) ✅ 유지 - This forward poppet will experience a maximum load that may be as much as 20–25% of the ship's weight when the stern lifts.
[줄 717] [97.6%] (40/41) ✅ 유지 - It is therefore designed to carry a load of this magnitude, but there is a danger in the fine-lined vessel of the forward poppets being forced outwards by the downward force, i.e the bow might break through the poppets.
[줄 718] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - To prevent this, cross ties or spreaders may be passed below the forefoot of the vessel and brackets may be temporarily fastened to the shell plating at the heads of the poppets.
[줄 719] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - In addition, saddle plates taken under the forefoot of the ship with packing between them and the shell may be fitted to transmit the load to the fore poppets and hence ground ways.
[줄 720] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In many modern ships the bow sections are relatively full and little support is required above the fore end of the sliding ways.
[줄 721] [100.0%] (6/6) ✅ 유지 - Here short plate brackets may be

[줄 726] [94.1%] (32/34) ✅ 유지 - Dry cargo ships If the development of the dry cargo ship from the time of introduction of steam propulsion is considered, the pattern of change is similar to that shown in Figure 3.2.
[줄 727] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - The first steam ships followed in most respects the design of the sailing ship, having a flush deck with the machinery openings protected only by low coamings and glass skylights.
[줄 728] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - At quite an early stage it was decided to protect the machinery openings with an enclosed bridge structure.
[줄 729] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Erections forming a forecastle and poop were also introduced at the forward and after respectively for protection.
[줄 730] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - This resulted in what is popularly known as the 'three island type'.
[줄 731] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - A number of designs at that time also combined bridge and poop, and a few combined bridge and forecastle, so that a single well was formed.
[줄 732] [100.0%] (10/10) ✅ 유지 - Another form of erection introduced was the raised quarter deck.
[줄 733] [78.6%] (11/14) ✅ 유지 - Raised quarter decks were often associated with smaller deadweight carrying vessels, e.g colliers.

[줄 735] [88.2%] (15/17) ✅ 유지 - temporarily welded between the shell plating and heavy plate wedge rider, as illustrated in Figure 15.2.
[줄 736] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - The design of the forward poppets is based on greater pressures than the lubricant between the sliding ways and ground ways could withstand if applied for any length of time.
[줄 737] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - However, as the duration of pivoting is small, and the vessel has sufficient momentum to prevent sticking at this stage, these high pressures are permissible.
[줄 738] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - At the after end of the cradle considerable packing may also be required, and again vertical timber props or plate brackets may be fitted to form the after poppet.
[줄 739] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Lubricant For the ship to start sliding on release of the holding arrangements, it is necessary for the ship to overcome the coefficient of friction of the launching lubricant.
[줄 740] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - To do this the slope of the ways under the vessel's center of gravity must exceed the lubricant's coefficient of friction.
[줄 741] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - An estimate of the frictional resistance of the grease must be made before building the ship, since the declivity of the keel is dependent to a large extent on the slope of the ways.
[줄 742] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Formerly, melted tallow was applied to the ways, allowed to harden, and then covered with a coat of soft soap.
[줄 743] [97.0%] (32/33) ✅ 유지 - Since the mid 1900s patent mineral-based greases have been applied to the ground ways, these greases being virtually unaffected by temperature changes and insoluble in water whilst adhering firmly to the ways.
[줄 744] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - A commercially marketed petroleum-based launching grease is applied over the mineral grease base coat.
[줄 745] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - This has a coefficient of friction that is low enough to allow initial starting and the maintenance of sliding until the initial resistance of the base coat is overcome by frictional heat.
[줄 746] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - To prevent the petroleum-based grease from soaking into the sliding ways, a base coat may be applied to them.
[줄 747] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Standing ways that extend into the water may be dried out at low tide prior to the launch and the base coat and grease applied.
[줄 748] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Releasing arrangements Small ships may be released by knocking away a diagonal dog-shore fitted between the sliding and standing ways.
[줄 749] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - In most cases, however, triggers are used to release the ship.
[줄 750] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - There are several types available, hydraulic, mechanical, and electrical-mechanical triggers having been used.
[줄 751] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Electrical-mechanical triggers are commonly used for rapid simultaneous release in modern practice.
[줄 752] [100.0%] (10/10) ✅ 유지 - The hydraulic trigger is less easily installed and less safe.
[줄 753] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - The electrical-mechanical trigger illustrated in Figure 15.3 is generally located near amidships and a small pit is provided in the berth to accommodate the falling levers.
[줄 754] [95.2%] (40/42) ✅ 유지 - A number of triggers will be fitted depending on the size of the vessel to be launched; in the case of the 75,000-tonne bulk carrier for which a launching sequence is given below, six triggers were fitted for the launch.
[줄 755] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - These triggers are in effect a simple system of levers that allow the large loads acting down the ways to be balanced by a small load on the releasing gear.
[줄 756] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - The principle is often compared with that of a simple mechanical reduction gearing.
[줄 757] [86.7%] (52/60) ✅ 유지 - FORE POPPET FOR SHIP WITH FULL FORWARD SECTIONS Plate bracket Plate ribband Ramming up wedges Make up Ground way Sliding way BRACKET IN WAY OF FRAMING Plate ribband Packing Sliding way Ground way Make up Ground way Sliding way Ribband Wedge Ribband Ribband Wood truss Bracket FORE POPPET FOR SHIP WITH FINE LINES FORWARD Figure 15.2 Launching waysfore poppet.
[줄 758] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Beam Dog shore Dog shore PLAN On sliding way On standing way Ground shore Steel shod Beam Sliding way ELEVATION Steel shod MECHANICAL LAUNCH TRIGGER
[줄 759] [80.0%] (20/25) ✅ 유지 - Sliding way Ground way 2nd lever Solenoid release unit Slip shackle 1st lever 3rd lever Load Anvil Figure 15.3 Release arrangements for ship launch.
[줄 760] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Simultaneous release of the triggers is achieved by means of catches held by solenoids wired in a common circuit.
[줄 761] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - These are released immediately the circuit current is reversed.
[줄 762] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - Launching sequence As a guide to the procedure leading up to the launch, the following example is given for the launch of a 75,000-tonne bulk carrier.
[줄 763] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The launch ways have been built up as the ship is erected from aft; the ways have been greased and the cradle erected.
[줄 764] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Four days before launch a start is made on ramming up the launch blocks, i.e driving in the wedges to raise ship off the building blocks.
[줄 765] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - This is done by a dozen or so men using a long ramming pole, a gang working either side of the ship.
[줄 766] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Two days before the launch a start is made on removing the shores.
[줄 767] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - On the morning of the launch everything is removed up to the high water mark and tumbler shores are put in aft.
[줄 768] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - These are inclined shores that fall away as the ship starts to move.
[줄 769] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - Every second keel block is then removed and the vessel is allowed to settle.
[줄 770] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - An evenly distributed number of keel blocks are then taken out so that only about 20 keel blocks are left supporting the ship.
[줄 771] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Half an hour before the launch the last remaining keel blocks are removed.
[줄 772] [100.0%] (6/6) ✅ 유지 - The bilge blocks are then removed.
[줄 773] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - The full ship's weight comes on the triggers at the time planned for the launch.
[줄 774] [100.0%] (7/7) ✅ 유지 - Release of triggers on launch by sponsor.
[줄 775] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - If the vessel fails to start under the action of gravity, the initial movement may be aided by hydraulic starting rams, which are provided at the head of the cradle.
[줄 776] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Arresting arrangements In many cases the extent of the water into which the ship is launched is restricted.
[줄 777] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - It is then necessary to provide means of arresting the motion of the ship once it is in the water.
[줄 778] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - There are a number of methods available for doing this, one or more being employed at most ship launches.
[줄 779] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - The commonest arrangement is to use chain drags, which are generally arranged symmetrically on either side of the ship.
[줄 780] [100.0%] (42/42) ✅ 유지 - Each chain drag is laid in the form of a horseshoe with its rounded portion away from the water, so that as the ship moves down the ways the forward portion of the drag is pulled through the remainder of the pile.
[줄 781] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - This prevents any excessive shock load in the chain, which would occur if the pile of chain were to be suddenly accelerated to the speed of the ship.
[줄 782] [94.4%] (34/36) ✅ 유지 - The wire rope drag lines are attached to temporary pads on the side of the ship, and supported by rope tricing lines as they are led slightly forward and then aft along the ship's sides.
[줄 783] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Each drag line is then led forward and shackled to the chain drag.
[줄 784] [92.0%] (23/25) ✅ 유지 - As the ship is released and moves aft the tricing lines are broken in turn, the work done absorbing some of the ship's energy.
[줄 785] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - To further increase the resistance to motion of the ship, wooden masks may be fitted at the stern of the ship.
[줄 786] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - The mask is made as large as possible but located low down to present a flat surface to the water in the direction of motion.
[줄 787] [100.0%] (3/3) ✅ 유지 - Masks are often
[줄 788] [87.9%] (29/33) ✅ 유지 - Welded pads Tricing lines Wire lines Cradle ELEVATION MASKS SECTION AFT LOOKING FOR'D Mask of wooden slats Way end PLAN Chain drags SLEWING ARRANGEMENTS Wire Figure 15.4 Arresting arrangements at launch.
[줄 789] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - constructed of horizontal pieces of wood with spaces left between each piece to increase the resistance.
[줄 790] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - One or two shipyards are forced to provide arrangements for slewing the vessel once it has left the ways, as the river into which the ships are launched is very narrow in relation to the ship's length.
[줄 791] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Chain drags, weights, or anchors may be placed in the water to one side of the building berth for this purpose.
[줄 792] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - These are then made fast to the stern of the ship with drag lines of a predetermined length.
[줄 793] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Once the vessel is clear of the ways the slack of the lines is taken up and the stern swings so that the ship is pointing up river.
[줄 794] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Side launches Side launching is often used where the width of water available is considerably restricted.
[줄 795] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - There are in fact some advantages to this method, for example the absence of keel declivity, and the relatively simple cradle and short ground ways that do not extend into the water.
[줄 796] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - However, it means that a large area of waterfront is taken up by a single building berth, and the ship is only reasonably accessible from one side during construction.
[줄 797] [94.1%] (16/17) ✅ 유지 - Side launching is usually restricted to small ships, typically no more that around 100 meters in length.
[줄 798] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - The ground ways are arranged transversely, i.e at right angles to the line of keel.
[줄 799] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Sliding ways can also be placed transversely with the packing above them forming the cradle, but they are generally arranged longitudinally.
[줄 800] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - In this case where they are parallel to the keel, the sliding ways are in groups covering two or three ground ways.
[줄 801] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - Packing again forms the cradle with tie pieces between the groups of sliding ways.
[줄 802] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - One of the features of side launching is the drop where the ground ways are not extended into the water; consequently, large angles of heel occur when the vessel strikes the water.
[줄 803] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - As a result it is necessary to carry out careful stability calculations and close any openings before side launching a vessel.
[줄 804] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - It is true, of course, that stability calculations are also required for a conventional end launch.
[줄 805] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Building docks Perhaps the greatest advantage of the building dock is the relative simplicity of the task of getting the vessel waterborne.
[줄 806] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - When it is convenient the dock may be flooded and the vessel floated out.
[줄 807] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - In a building dock it is also possible to construct two ships at the same time.
[줄 808] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - The second of two is usually at the landward end of the dock, and can be separated from the seaward end by an intermediate dock gate.
[줄 809] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - The first ship can then be floated out of the dock while the second remains in the dry.
[줄 810] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - Once the dock is dewatered the second ship can be moved to the seaward end and a third ship started.
[줄 811] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - This allows better utilization of the large and expensive cranes, and also allows double the time to complete the more outfit-intensive zones of the ship, usually the aft machinery spaces and accommodation.
[줄 812] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - The dock also has a horizontal base, which simplifies alignment of structural units or blocks and management of the ship dimensions.
[줄 813] [97.2%] (35/36) ✅ 유지 - Calculations are needed to check the stability and loads exerted by the blocks during flooding, the whole problem being similar to that of undocking a vessel that has been dry-docked for survey or other reasons.
[줄 814] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - In some shipyards conventional berths are fitted at the river or sea end with what is virtually a pair of dock gates.
[줄 815] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - This can be of advantage when working the aft end of the ship and installing the ways.
[줄 816] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - In many instances it also permits higher tides over the way ends when the gates are opened for a launch.
[줄 817] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - A dock gate is ideal in tideless conditions, for example in the Baltic or Mediterranean Seas.
[줄 818] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - The ship can be built with the gate closed, maintaining a dry working environment.
[줄 819] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - When the gate is opened the lower part of the slipway floods and provides sufficient water depth for the launch to be carried out successfully.
[줄 820] [100.0%] (47/47) ✅ 유지 - Whilst large ships may be extruded out of building halls on to a slipway and large sections transferred by similar means to the head of the slipway and raised onto it for joining and launching, smaller complete ships may be transferred to a ship lift for launching.
[줄 821] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Rail systems are incorporated into the building hall and lead out to the open ship lift.
[줄 822] [96.9%] (31/32) ✅ 유지 - The best known of these ship lift systems is the patented 'Syncrolift', originally used for slipping ships for repairs and surveys but now also used by some shipyards for launching new ships.
[줄 823] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Ship lifts basically consist of a series of transverse beams, each supported by wires or chains suspended from a winch on each side.
[줄 824] [100.0%] (10/10) ✅ 유지 - The beams have the transfer rails running longitudinally across them.
[줄 825] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - A platform is also supported by the beams to provide access when the ship is lifted clear of the water.
[줄 826] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - To launch, the ship is positioned on the structure, which can be lowered into the water and the ship floated off the platform.
[줄 827] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - The lift can also be used to recover a ship from the water for repair.
[줄 828] [100.0%] (36/36) ✅ 유지 - The platform is raised and lowered mechanically or hydraulically and is usually provided with transfer arrangements so that the vessel can be moved on or off the platform either laterally or in line with the platform.
[줄 829] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Originally, ship lifts were used for fleets of small ships, for example in fishing ports, but have increased in size for large commercial repairs and some construction.
[줄 830] [81.8%] (9/11) ✅ 유지 - The largest lift is able to lift over 20,000 tonnes.
[줄 831] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Floating docks Occasionally, and usually as a temporary expedient, a ship can be built on the land and transferred to a floating dock for launching.
[줄 832] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - The arrangement is similar to a ship lift, with rails to allow the completed ship to be transferred onto the dock.
[줄 833] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - The dock is then sunk in the location or may be towed to deeper water so the ship can be floated off.
[줄 834] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - As an alternative a ship may be transferred to a pontoon, in an operation similar to an offshore structure loadout.
[줄 835] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The pontoon will require some reserve buoyancy to maintain stability during the operation and this is usually provided by 'towers' at each corner.
[줄 836] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Such a specialized pontoon is less expensive than a conventional floating dock.
[줄 837] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Marine railways A few small shipyards use a slipway with a set or rails that extend into the water.
[줄 838] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - The ship is constructed on, or transferred to, a cradle that can run on the rails.
[줄 839] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - For launch, the cradle is lowered down the slipway until the ship floats off.
[줄 840] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - The operation is under control, unlike a dynamic end launch where, once started, the ship cannot be stopped.
[줄 841] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - As with the ship lift, a marine railway can also be used to recover ships for repair.
[줄 842] [81.8%] (9/11) ✅ 유지 - Further reading Dunn, Kennedy, and Tibbs, Launching in the 21st century.
[줄 843] [75.0%] (9/12) ✅ 유지 - The Royal Institution of Naval Architects, Drydocks, Launching and Shiplift Conference, 2003.
[줄 844] [81.8%] (9/11) ✅ 유지 - Pattison, Dixon, and Hodder, Launching and docking: Experiences at VT shipbuilding.
[줄 845] [75.0%] (9/12) ✅ 유지 - The Royal Institution of Naval Architects, Drydocks, Launching and Shiplift Conference, 2003.
[줄 846] [84.6%] (11/13) ✅ 유지 - Salisbury and Dobb, Recent dynamic launches at Barrow in Furness: Prediction and reality.
[줄 847] [75.0%] (9/12) ✅ 유지 - The Royal Institution of Naval Architects, Drydocks, Launching and Shiplift Conference, 2003.

[줄 850] [92.3%] (24/26) ✅ 유지 - Testing double-bottom compartments 184 Machinery seats 184 Originally, ships were constructed with single bottoms, liquid fuels and fresh water being contained within separately constructed tanks.
[줄 851] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - The double-bottom structure, which provides increased safety in the event of bottom shell damage, and also provides liquid tank space low down in the ship, evolved during the early part of the twentieth century.
[줄 852] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Today, only small vessels such as tugs, ferries, and cargo ships of less than 500 gross tonnage have a single-bottom construction.
[줄 853] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Larger ocean-going vessels are fitted with some form of double bottom.
[줄 854] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Keels At the center line of the bottom structure is located the keel, which is often said to form the backbone of the ship.
[줄 855] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - This contributes substantially to the longitudinal strength and effectively distributes local loading caused when docking the ship.
[줄 856] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - The commonest form of keel is that known as the 'flat plate' keel, and this is fitted in the majority of ocean-going and other vessels.
[줄 857] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - A form of keel found on smaller vessels is the bar keel.
[줄 858] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - The bar keel may be fitted in trawlers, tugs, etc and is also found in smaller ferries.
[줄 859] [96.6%] (28/29) ✅ 유지 - Where grounding is possible this type of keel is suitable with its massive scantlings, but there is always a problem of the increased draft with no additional cargo capacity.
[줄 860] [100.0%] (39/39) ✅ 유지 - If a double bottom is fitted the keel is almost inevitably of the flat plate type, and bar keels are more often associated with open floors, but a flat plate keel can be fitted in way of open floors.

[줄 868] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - Duct keels are provided in the double bottoms of some vessels.
[줄 869] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - These run from the forward engine room bulkhead to the collision bulkhead and are utilized to carry the double-bottom piping.
[줄 870] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - The piping is then accessible when cargo is loaded, an entrance to the duct being provided at the forward end of the engine room.
[줄 871] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - No duct is required aft of the engine room as the piping may be carried in the shaft tunnel.
[줄 872] [87.9%] (29/33) ✅ 유지 - Awidth of not more than 2.0 m is allowed for the duct, and strengthening is provided at the tank top and keel plate to maintain continuity of strength of the transverse floors.
[줄 873] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Single-bottom structure In smaller ships having single bottoms the vertical plate open floors are fitted at every frame space and are stiffened at their upper edge.
[줄 874] [88.7%] (55/62) ✅ 유지 - A center-line girder is fitted and one side girder is fitted each side of the center line where the beam is less than 10 m Where the beam is between 10 and 17 m, two side girders are fitted and if any bottom shell panel has a width-to-length ratio greater than 4 additional continuous or intercostal stiffeners are fitted.
[줄 875] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - The continuous center and intercostal side girders are stiffened at their upper edge and extend as far forward and aft as possible.
[줄 876] [87.1%] (27/31) ✅ 유지 - The single-bottom structure is shown in Figure 16.2 and for clarity a threedimensional representation of the structure is also provided to illustrate those members that are continuous or intercostal.
[줄 877] [93.1%] (27/29) ✅ 유지 - Both single and double bottoms have continuous and intercostal material, and there is often some confusion in the student's mind as to what is implied by these terms.
[줄 878] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - Awood ceiling may be fitted across the top of the floors if cargoes are to be carried, but this does not constitute an inner bottom offering any protection if the outer bottom shell is damaged.
[줄 879] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Double-bottom structure An inner bottom may be provided at a minimum height above the bottom shell, and maintained watertight to the bilges.
[줄 880] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - This provides a considerable margin of safety, since in the event of bottom shell damage only the double-bottom space may be flooded.
[줄 881] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - The space is not wasted but utilized to carry oil fuel and fresh water required for the ship, as well as providing ballast capacity.
[줄 882] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - The minimum depth of the double bottom in a ship will depend on the classification society's requirement for the depth of center girder.
[줄 883] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - It may be deeper to give the required capacities of oil fuel, fresh water, and water ballast to be carried in the bottom.
[줄 884] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Water-ballast bottom tanks are commonly provided right forward and aft for trimming purposes and if necessary the depth of the double bottom may be increased in these regions.
[줄 885] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In way of the machinery spaces the double-bottom depth is also increased to provide appreciable capacities of lubricating oil and fuel oil.
[줄 886] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - The increase in height of the inner bottom is always by a gradual taper in the longitudinal direction, no sudden discontinuities in the structure being tolerated.
[줄 887] [85.7%] (30/35) ✅ 유지 - ELEVATION Intercostal side girder Flange Floor Flange Intercostal side girder LOOKING FOR'D Solid floor Center girder Bar keel Ships Manhole OPEN FLOORS Flange Fore and aft intercostal side keelsons Center girder Transverse plate floors
[줄 888] [60.0%] (6/10) ✅ 유지 - Garboard strake Bar keel Figure 16.2 Single-bottom construction.
[줄 889] [88.0%] (22/25) ✅ 유지 - Double bottoms may be framed longitudinally or transversely, but where the ship's length exceeds 120 m it is considered desirable to adopt longitudinal framing.
[줄 890] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - The explanation for this is that on longer ships tests and experience have shown that there is a tendency for the inner bottom and bottom shell to buckle if welded transverse framing is adopted.
[줄 891] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - This buckling occurs as a result of the longitudinal bending of the hull, and may be avoided by having the plating longitudinally stiffened.

[줄 894] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Double bottoms in the way of machinery spaces that are adjacent to the after peak are required to be transversely framed.
[줄 895] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Inner bottom plating The inner bottom plating may, in a general cargo ship, be sloped at the side to form a bilge for drainage purposes.
[줄 896] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - It is not uncommon, however, for it to be extended to the ship's side, and individual bilge wells are then provided for drainage purposes.
[줄 897] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - In vessels requiring a passenger certificate it is a statutory requirement for the tank top to extend to the ship's side.
[줄 898] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - This provides a greater degree of safety, since there is a substantial area of bilge that may be damaged without flooding spaces above the inner bottom.
[줄 899] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - At the center line of the ship the middle strake of the inner bottom may be considered as the upper flange of the center-line docking girder, formed by the center girder and keel plate.
[줄 900] [92.3%] (12/13) ✅ 유지 - It may therefore be heavier than the other strakes of inner bottom plating.
[줄 901] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Normally, a wood ceiling is provided under a hatchway in a general cargo ship, but the inner bottom plating thickness can be increased and the ceiling omitted.
[줄 902] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - If grabs are used for discharging from general cargo ships the plate thickness is further increased, or a double ceiling is fitted.
[줄 903] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Floors Vertical transverse plate floors are provided both where the bottom is transversely and longitudinally framed.
[줄 904] [94.7%] (18/19) ✅ 유지 - At the ends of bottom tank spaces and under the main bulkheads, watertight or oiltight plate floors are provided.
[줄 905] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - These are made watertight or oiltight by closing any holes in the plate floor and welding collars around any members that pass through the floors.
[줄 906] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Elsewhere, 'solid plate floors' are fitted to strengthen the bottom transversely and support the inner bottom.
[줄 907] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - These run transversely from the continuous center girder to the bilge, and manholes provided for access through the tanks and lightening holes are cut in each solid plate floor.
[줄 908] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Also, small air and drain holes may be drilled at the top and bottom respectively of the solid plate floors in the tank spaces.
[줄 909] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - The spacing of the solid plate floors varies according to the loads supported and local stresses experienced.
[줄 910] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - At intermediate frame spaces between the solid plate floors, 'bracket floors' are fitted.
[줄 911] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - The bracket floor consists simply of short transverse plate brackets fitted in way of the center girder and tank sides.
[줄 912] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - Transversely framed double bottom If the double bottom is transversely framed, then transverse solid plate floors, and bracket floors with transverse frames, provide the principal support for the inner bottom and bottom shell plating.
[줄 913] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Solid plate floors are fitted at every frame space in the engine room and in the pounding region.
[줄 914] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - Also, they are introduced in way of boiler seats, transverse bulkheads, toes of brackets supporting stiffeners on deep tank bulkheads, and in way of any change in depth of the double

[줄 921] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Where a ship is regularly discharged by grabs, solid plate floors are also fitted at each frame.
[줄 922] [87.5%] (21/24) ✅ 유지 - Elsewhere, the solid plate floors may be spaced up to 3.0 m apart, with bracket floors at frame spaces between the solid floors.
[줄 923] [92.3%] (24/26) ✅ 유지 - The plate brackets of bracket floors are flanged and their breadth is at least 75% of the depth of the center girder at the bracket floors.
[줄 924] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - To reduce the span of the frames, which should not exceed 2.5 meters, at the bracket floor, vertical angle or channel bar struts may be fitted.
[줄 925] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - Vertical stiffeners, usually in the form of welded flats, will be attached to the solid plate floors, which are further strengthened if they form a watertight or oiltight tank boundary.
[줄 926] [81.1%] (30/37) ✅ 유지 - One intercostal side girder is provided port and starboard where the ship's breadth exceeds 10 m but does not exceed 20 m, and two are fitted port and starboard where the ship's breadth is greater.
[줄 927] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - In way of the bracket floors a vertical welded flat stiffener is attached to the side girder.
[줄 928] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - Additional side girders are provided in the engine room, and also in the pounding region.
[줄 929] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Longitudinally framed double bottom In a longitudinally framed double bottom, solid plate floors are fitted at every frame space under the main engines, and at alternate frames outboard of the engine seating.
[줄 930] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - They are also fitted under boiler seats, transverse bulkheads, and the toes of stiffener brackets on deep tank bulkheads.
[줄 931] [88.0%] (22/25) ✅ 유지 - Elsewhere, the spacing of solid plate floors does not exceed 3.8 m, except in the pounding region, where they are on alternate frame spaces.
[줄 932] [88.5%] (23/26) ✅ 유지 - At intermediate frame spaces brackets are fitted at the tank side and at the center girder, where they may be up to 1.25 m apart.
[줄 933] [90.9%] (10/11) ✅ 유지 - Each bracket is flanged and will extend to the first longitudinal.
[줄 934] [80.0%] (24/30) ✅ 유지 - One intercostal side girder is fitted port and starboard if the ship's breadth exceeds 14 m, and where the breadth exceeds 21 m two are fitted port and starboard.
[줄 935] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - These side girders always extend as far forward and aft as possible.
[줄 936] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Additional side girders are provided in the engine room and under the main machinery, and they should run the full length of the engine room, extending three frame spaces beyond this space.
[줄 937] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - Forward, the extension tapers into the longitudinal framing system.
[줄 938] [91.7%] (11/12) ✅ 유지 - In the pounding region there will also be additional intercostal side girders.
[줄 939] [84.4%] (27/32) ✅ 유지 - As the unsupported span of the bottom longitudinals should not exceed 2.5 m, vertical angle or channel bar struts may be provided to support the longitudinals between widely spaced solid floors.
[줄 940] [87.7%] (50/57) ✅ 유지 - Additional stiffening in the pounding region If the minimum designed draft forward in any ballast or part-loaded condition is less than 4.5% of the ship's length, then the bottom structure for 30% of the ship's length forward in sea-going ships exceeding 65 m in length is to be additionally strengthened for pounding.
[줄 941] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Where the double bottom is transversely framed, solid plate floors are fitted at every frame space in the pounding region.
[줄 942] [93.5%] (29/31) ✅ 유지 - Intercostal side girders are fitted at a maximum spacing of three times the transverse floor spacing, and half-height intercostal side girders are provided midway between the full-height side girders.
[줄 943] [94.2%] (49/52) ✅ 유지 - If the double bottom is longitudinally framed in the pounding region, where the minimum designed draft forward may be less than 4% of the ship's length, solid plate floors are fitted at alternate frame spaces, and intercostal side girders fitted at a maximum spacing of three times the transverse floor spacing.
[줄 944] [89.6%] (43/48) ✅ 유지 - Where the minimum designed draft forward may be more than 4% but less than 4.5% of the ship's length, solid plate floors may be fitted at every third frame space and intercostal side girders may have a maximum spacing of four times the transverse floor spacing.
[줄 945] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - As longitudinals are stiffening the bottom shell longitudinally, it should be noted that fewer side girders need be provided than where the bottom is transversely framed to resist distortion of the bottom with the slamming forces experienced.
[줄 946] [92.0%] (23/25) ✅ 유지 - Where the ballast draft forward is less than 1% of the ship's length, the additional strengthening of the pounding region is given special consideration.
[줄 947] [97.6%] (40/41) ✅ 유지 - Greater slamming forces i.e pounding are experienced when the ship is in the lighter ballast condition, and is long and slender, by reason of the increased submersion of the bow in heavy weather with impact also on the bow flare.
[줄 948] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Bottom structure of bulk carriers Where a ship is classed for the carriage of heavy, or ore, cargoes longitudinal framing is adopted for the double bottom.
[줄 949] [77.4%] (24/31) ✅ 유지 - A closer spacing of solid plate floors is required, the maximum spacing being 2.5 m, and also additional intercostal side girders are provided, the spacing not exceeding 3.7 m.
[줄 950] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - The double bottom will be somewhat deeper than in a conventional cargo ship, a considerable ballast capacity being required, and often a pipe tunnel is provided through this space.
[줄 951] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - Inner bottom plating, floors, and girders all have substantial scantlings as a result of the heavier cargo weights to be supported.
[줄 952] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - Testing double-bottom compartments Each compartment is tested on completion with a head of water representing the maximum pressure head that may be experienced in service, i.e to the top of the air pipe.
[줄 953] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Alternatively, air testing is carried out before any protective coatings are applied.
[줄 954] [76.0%] (19/25) ✅ 유지 - The air pressure may be raised to 0.21 kg/cm 2 and then lowered to a test pressure of 0.14 kg/cm 2.
[줄 955] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Any suspect joints are then subjected to a soapy liquid solution test.
[줄 956] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Water head structural tests will be carried out on tanks selected by the surveyor in conjunction with the air tests carried out on the majority of tanks.
[줄 957] [97.1%] (33/34) ✅ 유지 - Machinery seats It has already been indicated that in the machinery spaces additional transverse floors and longitudinal intercostal side girders are provided to support the machinery effectively and to ensure rigidity of the structure.
[줄 958] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - The main engine seatings are in general integral with this double-bottom structure, and the inner bottom in way of the engine foundation has a substantially increased

[줄 975] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - The shell plating forms the watertight skin of the ship and at the same time, in merchant ship construction, contributes to the longitudinal strength and resists vertical shear forces.
[줄 976] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Internal strengthening of the shell plating may be both transverse and longitudinal, and is designed to prevent collapse of the plating under the various loads to which it is subjected.
[줄 977] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Shell plating The bottom and side shell plating consists of a series of flat and curved steel plates generally of greater length than breadth butt welded together.
[줄 978] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - The vertical welded joints are referred to as 'butts' and the horizontal welded joints as 'seams'.
[줄 979] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Stiffening members both longitudinal and transverse are generally welded to the shell by continuous fillet welds.
[줄 980] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - Framing is notched in way of welded plate butts and seams.
[줄 981] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Bottom shell plating Throughout the length of the ship the width and thickness of the keel plate remain constant where a flat plate keel is fitted.
[줄 982] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Its thickness is never less than that of the adjoining bottom plating.
[줄 983] [88.5%] (23/26) ✅ 유지 - Strakes of bottom plating to the bilges have their greatest thickness over the 40% of the ship's length amidships, where the bending stresses are highest.
[줄 984] [100.0%] (4/4) ✅ 유지 - The bottom Ship Construction.
[줄 985] [100.0%] (3/3) ✅ 유지 - All rights reserved.
[줄 986] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - plating then tapers to a lesser thickness at the ends of the ship, apart from increased thickness requirements in way of the pounding region.
[줄 987] [91.9%] (34/37) ✅ 유지 - Side shell plating As with the bottom shell plating, the greater thickness of the side shell plating is maintained within 40% of the vessel's midship length and then tapers to the rule thickness at the ends.
[줄 988] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - The thickness may be increased in regions where high vertical shear stresses occur, usually in way of transverse bulkheads in a vessel permitted to carry heavy cargoes with some holds empty.
[줄 989] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - There is also a thickness increase at the stern frame connection, at any shaft brackets, and in way of the hawse pipes, where considerable chafing occurs.
[줄 990] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Further shell plate thickness increases may be found at the panting region, as discussed later in this chapter.
[줄 991] [87.5%] (14/16) ✅ 유지 - The upper strake of plating adjacent to the strength deck is referred to as the 'sheerstrake'.
[줄 992] [92.0%] (23/25) ✅ 유지 - As the sheerstrake is at a large distance from the neutral axis it has a greater thickness than the other strakes of side shell plating.
[줄 993] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - Also, being in a highly stressed region it is necessary to avoid welded attachments to the sheerstrake, or cutouts that would introduce stress raisers.
[줄 994] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - The upper edge is dressed smooth, and the welding of bulwarks to the edge of the sheerstrake is not permitted within the amidships length of the ship.
[줄 995] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Scupper openings above the deck over the same length, and at the ends of the superstructure, are also prohibited in larger vessels.
[줄 996] [96.4%] (27/28) ✅ 유지 - The connection between the sheerstrake and strength deck can present a problem, and a rounded gunwale may be adopted to solve this problem where the plating is heavy.
[줄 997] [93.3%] (14/15) ✅ 유지 - This is often the case over the midship portion of large tankers and bulk carriers.
[줄 998] [96.6%] (28/29) ✅ 유지 - Butt welds are then employed to make connections rather than the less satisfactory fillet weld at the perpendicular connection of the vertical sheerstrake and horizontal strength deck stringer plate.
[줄 999] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - The radius of a rounded gunwale must be adequate and any welded guardrails and fairleads are kept off the radiused plate if possible.
[줄 1000] [88.0%] (22/25) ✅ 유지 - 25mm Rad notch cut in frame in way of seam Welded seam One frame space Frame Welded butt Welded butt Figure 17.1 Shell plating.
[줄 1001] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - A smooth transition from rounded gunwale to angled sheerstrake/deck stringer connection is necessary at the ends of the ship.
[줄 1002] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - All openings in the side shell have rounded corners, and openings for sea inlets etc are kept clear of the bilge radius if possible.
[줄 1003] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Where this is not possible openings on or in the vicinity of the bilge are made elliptical.
[줄 1004] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Grades of steel for shell plates In large ships it is necessary to arrange strakes of steel with greater notch ductility at the more highly stressed regions.
[줄 1005] [83.3%] (20/24) ✅ 유지 - Details of Lloyd's requirements for mild steel and over 40% of the length amidships are given in Table 17.1 as a guide.
[줄 1006] [91.7%] (22/24) ✅ 유지 - The rules also require thicker plating for the members referred to in Table 17.1 outside the amidships region to have greater notch ductility.
[줄 1007] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - Framing The bottom shell may be transversely or longitudinally framed, longitudinal framing being preferred for larger ships, and generally required when the ship's length exceeds 120 meters.
[줄 1008] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - The side shell framing may also be transversely or longitudinally framed, transverse framing being adopted in many conventional cargo ships, particularly where the maximum bale capacity is required.
[줄 1009] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - Bale capacities are often considerably reduced where deep transverses are fitted to support longitudinal framing.
[줄 1010] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Longitudinal framing is adopted within double-hull spaces and is common within the hopper and topside tanks of bulk carriers.
[줄 1011] [77.8%] (14/18) ✅ 유지 - Smaller single-skin bulk carriers Table 17.1 Lloyd's requirements for mild steel Requirement Structural member 1.
[줄 1012] [75.0%] (21/28) ✅ 유지 - Grade D where thickness is less than 15 mm, otherwise Grade E Sheerstrake or rounded gunwale over 40% of length amidships in ships exceeding 250 m in length.

[줄 1026] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - Transverse framing In a general cargo ship the transverse framing will consist of main and hold frames with brackets top and bottom, and lighter tween deck frames with brackets at the tops only.
[줄 1027] [80.0%] (12/15) ✅ 유지 - A typical midship section for a general cargo ship is shown in Figure 17.6.
[줄 1028] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - Deck beam Tween frame Deck beam Hold frame Web frame Tank side bracket Beam knee Figure 17.2 Side shell with transverse framing.
[줄 1029] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - Scantlings of the main transverse frames are primarily dependent on their position, spacing and depth, and to some extent on the rigidity of the end connections.
[줄 1030] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - In way of tanks such as oil bunkers or cargo deep tanks the side frame size will be increased, except where supporting side stringers are fitted within the tank space.
[줄 1031] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Frames supporting hatch end beams and those in way of deck transverses, where the deck is framed longitudinally, also have increased scantlings.
[줄 1032] [96.9%] (31/32) ✅ 유지 - Web frames, i.e built-up frames consisting of plate web and face flat, where the web is considerably deeper than the conventional transverse frame, are often introduced along the side shell.
[줄 1033] [96.4%] (27/28) ✅ 유지 - A number are fitted in midship machinery spaces, generally not more than five frame spaces apart, but may be omitted if the size of normal framing is increased.
[줄 1034] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - Forward of the collision bulkhead and in any deep tank adjacent to the collision bulkhead, and in tween decks above such tanks, web frames are required at not more than five frame spaces apart.
[줄 1035] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In the tween decks above the after peak tank, web frames are required at every fourth frame space abaft the aft peak bulkhead.
[줄 1036] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - In all cases the provision of web frames is intended to increase the rigidity of the transverse ship section at that point.
[줄 1037] [93.3%] (14/15) ✅ 유지 - Longitudinal framing The longitudinal framing of the bottom shell is dealt with in Chapter 16.
[줄 1038] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - If the side shell is longitudinally framed offset bulb sections will often be employed with the greater section scantlings at the lower side shell.
[줄 1039] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Direct continuity of strength is to be maintained, and many of the details are similar to those illustrated for the tanker longitudinals.
[줄 1040] [82.9%] (29/35) ✅ 유지 - Transverse webs are fitted to support the side longitudinals, these being spaced not more than 3.8 m apart, in ships of 100 m length or less, with increasing spacing being permitted for longer ships.
[줄 1041] [85.1%] (57/67) ✅ 유지 - In the peaks the spacing is 2.5 m where the length of ship is less than 100 m, increasing linearly to a spacing of 3.5 m where the length exceeds 300 m Larger ships required to have a double hull are longitudinally framed at the sides with transverse webs arranged in line with the floors in the double bottom to ensure continuity of transverse strength.
[줄 1042] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Horizontal perforated flats are fitted between the inner and outer side plating to support the transverse webs.
[줄 1043] [78.6%] (11/14) ✅ 유지 - A roll on roll off ship midship section is shown in Figure 17.10.
[줄 1044] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - This is also longitudinally framed, and the side casing is similar to the double hull of other types.
[줄 1045] [87.5%] (14/16) ✅ 유지 - Avery different ship type is shown in Figure 17.11, that is a catamaran fast ferry.
[줄 1046] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - The hull form is radically different and the material for construction is aluminium, to minimize the weight of the structure.
[줄 1047] [83.3%] (15/18) ✅ 유지 - The basic longitudinal framing, with transverse webs, ishoweveressentially the same asfor the other shiptypes described in this chapter.
[줄 1048] [89.5%] (34/38) ✅ 유지 - Tank side brackets The lower end of the frame may be connected to the tank top or hopper side tank by means of a flanged or edge-stiffened tank side bracket, as illustrated in Figure 17.3 b.
[줄 1049] [92.4%] (61/66) ✅ 유지 - Stiffener Solid floor Solid floor Solid floor Tank side bracket Stiffener Lightening hole Hold frame Tank top Hold frame TANK SIDE BRACKETS OR CONNECTIONS Tank top Flat stiffener 200mm flat facing bar WEB FRAME 750 mm Deck transverse Tween frame Tween deck Deck longitudinals Web plate Solid floor Tank side bracket Margin plate Hold frame Flange Flange Figure 17.3 Web frame and tank side bracket.
[줄 1050] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Local strengthening of shell plating The major region in which the shell plating is subjected to local forces at sea is at the forward end.
[줄 1051] [93.3%] (14/15) ✅ 유지 - Strengthening of the forward bottom shell for pounding forces is dealt with in Chapter 16.
[줄 1052] [93.3%] (28/30) ✅ 유지 - Panting, which is discussed in Chapter 8, will also influence the requirements for the scantlings and strengthening of the shell forward and to a lesser extent at the aft end.
[줄 1053] [100.0%] (36/36) ✅ 유지 - Where a ship is to navigate in ice, a special classification may be assigned depending on the type and severity of ice encountered, and this will involve strengthening the shell forward and in the waterline region.
[줄 1054] [93.6%] (44/47) ✅ 유지 - Additional stiffening for panting Additional stiffening is provided in the fore peak structure, the transverse side framing being supported by any, or a combination of the following arrangements: 1 Side stringers spaced vertically about 2 m apart and supported by struts or beams fitted at alternate frames.
[줄 1055] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - These 'panting beams' are connected to the frames by brackets and if long may be supported at the ship's center line by a partial wash bulkhead.
[줄 1056] [100.0%] (7/7) ✅ 유지 - Intermediate frames are bracketed to the stringer.
[줄 1057] [84.6%] (11/13) ✅ 유지 - Side stringers spaced vertically about 2 m apart and supported by web frames.
[줄 1058] [70.0%] (7/10) ✅ 유지 - Perforated flats spaced not more than 2.5 m apart.
[줄 1059] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - The area of perforations is not less than 10% of the total area of the flat.
[줄 1060] [94.7%] (36/38) ✅ 유지 - Aft of the forepeak in the lower hold or deep tank spaces panting stringers are fitted in line with each stringer or perforated flat in the fore peak extending back over 15% of the ship length from forward.
[줄 1061] [83.3%] (30/36) ✅ 유지 - These stringers may be omitted if the shell plating thickness is increased by 15% for vessels of 150 m length or less, decreasing linearly to a 5% increase for vessels of 215 m length or more.
[줄 1062] [91.3%] (42/46) ✅ 유지 - However, where the unsupported length of the main frames exceeds 9 m, panting stringers in line with alternate stringers or flats in the fore peak are to be fitted over 20% of the ship's length from forward whether the shell thickness is increased or not.
[줄 1063] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Stringers usually take the form of a web plate with flat facing bar.
[줄 1064] [82.5%] (33/40) ✅ 유지 - In tween deck spaces in the forward 15% of the ship's length, intermediate panting stringers are fitted where the unsupported length of tween frame exceeds 2.6 m in lower tween decks or 3 m in upper tween decks.
[줄 1065] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - Alternatively, the shell thickness may be increased as above.
[줄 1066] [92.1%] (35/38) ✅ 유지 - In the aft peak space and in deep tween decks above the aft peak similar panting arrangements are required for transverse framing, except that the vertical spacing of panting stringers may be up to 2.5 m apart.
[줄 1067] [91.7%] (33/36) ✅ 유지 - If the fore peak has longitudinal framing and the depth of tank exceeds 10 m the transverse webs supporting the longitudinals are to be supported by perforated flats or an arrangement of transverse struts or beams.
[줄 1068] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Strengthening for navigation in ice If a vessel is to be assigned a special features notation for navigation in first-year ice, the additional strengthening required involves primarily an increase

[줄 1072] [94.3%] (33/35) ✅ 유지 - A main ice belt zone is defined that extends above the ice load waterline i.e normally the summer load waterline and below the ice light waterline i.e lightest waterline ship navigates ice in.
[줄 1073] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - The extent of this zone depends on the ice class assigned.
[줄 1074] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - The shell plating thickness in this zone is greater than on a conventional ship and increases with severity of ice class and with position from aft to forward.
[줄 1075] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - For the more severe ice conditions the thickness of the side shell is also increased below the main ice belt zone for at least 40% of the length from forward.
[줄 1076] [94.4%] (17/18) ✅ 유지 - Transverse main and intermediate frames of heavier scantlings are fitted in way of the main ice belt zone.
[줄 1077] [89.5%] (17/19) ✅ 유지 - Where the shell is longitudinally framed, longitudinals of increased scantlings are fitted in way of the ice belt zone.
[줄 1078] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Both transverse and longitudinal frame scantling requirements are dependent on the severity of ice class assigned and distance of frame from forward.
[줄 1079] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - Transverse ice framing is supported by ice stringers and decks, and longitudinal framing by web frames, the scantlings of which are increased with severity of ice class and distance from forward.
[줄 1080] [100.0%] (45/45) ✅ 유지 - Strengthening for addition of 'Icebreaker' notation to ship-type notation and assignment of special features notation for navigation in multi-year ice and the associated requirements for plating and framing at the bow and stern are too extensive to be covered adequately in this text.
[줄 1081] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Bilge keel Most ships are fitted with some form of bilge keel, the prime function of which is to help damp the rolling motion of the vessel.
[줄 1082] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Other relatively minor advantages of the bilge keel are protection for the bilge on grounding, and increased longitudinal strength at the bilge.
[줄 1083] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The damping action provided by the bilge keel is relatively small but effective, and virtually without cost after the construction of the ship.
[줄 1084] [100.0%] (43/43) ✅ 유지 - It is carefully positioned on the ship so as to avoid excessive drag when the ship is under way, and to achieve a minimum drag, various positions of the bilge keel may be tested on the ship model used to predict power requirements.
[줄 1085] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - This bilge keel then generally runs over the midship portion of the hull, often extending further aft than forward of amidships and being virtually perpendicular to the turn of the bilge.
[줄 1086] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - There are many forms of bilge keel construction, and some quite elaborate arrangements have been adopted in an attempt to improve the damping performance whilst reducing any drag.
[줄 1087] [100.0%] (43/43) ✅ 유지 - Care is required in the design of the bilge keel, for although it would not be considered as a critical strength member of the hull structure, the region of its attachment is fairly highly stressed owing to its distance from the neutral axis.
[줄 1088] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Cracks have originated in the bilge keel and propagated into the bilge plate causing failure of the main structure.
[줄 1089] [100.0%] (7/7) ✅ 유지 - In general, bilge keels are attached to
[줄 1090] [100.0%] (7/7) ✅ 유지 - wells for the protection of these cargoes.
[줄 1091] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - This resulted in the awning or spar deck type of ship, the temporary enclosed spaces being exempt from tonnage measurement since they were not permanently closed spaces.
[줄 1092] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - These awning or spar deck structures eventually became an integral part of the ship structure but retained a lighter structure than the upper deck structure of other two-deck ships, later referred to as 'full scantling' vessels.
[줄 1093] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - The 'shelter deck type', as this form of vessel became known, apart from having a lighter upper structure was to have the freeboard measured from the second deck, and the tween deck space was exempt from tonnage measurement.
[줄 1094] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - This exemption was obtained by the provision of openings in the shelter deck and tween deck bulkheads complying with certain statutory regulations.
[줄 1095] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - At a later date, what were known as open/closed shelter deck ships were developed.
[줄 1096] [94.6%] (35/37) ✅ 유지 - These were full scantling ships having the prescribed openings so that the tween deck was exempt from tonnage measurement when the vessel was operating at a load draft where the freeboard was measured from the second deck.
[줄 1097] [97.6%] (41/42) ✅ 유지 - It was possible to close permanently these temporary openings and reassign the freeboard, it then being measured from the upper deck so that the vessel might load to a deeper draft, and the tween deck was no longer exempt from tonnage measurement.
[줄 1098] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Open shelter deck vessels were popular with shipowners for a long period.
[줄 1099] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - However, during that time much consideration was given to their safety and the undesirable form of temporary openings in the main hull structure.
[줄 1100] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Eliminating these openings without substantially altering the tonnage values was the object of much discussion and deliberation.
[줄 1101] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Finally, Tonnage Regulations introduced in 1966 provided for the assignment of a tonnage mark, at a stipulated distance below the second deck.
[줄 1102] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - A vessel having a 'modified tonnage' had tonnage measured to the second deck only, i.e the tween deck was exempt, but the tonnage mark was not to be submerged.
[줄 1103] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Where a vessel was assigned 'alternative tonnages', tonnage was taken as that to the second deck when the tonnage mark was not submerged.
[줄 1104] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - When the tonnage mark was submerged, tonnage was taken as that to the upper deck, the freeboard being a minimum measured from the upper deck.
[줄 1105] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - The tonnage mark concept effectively dispensed with the undesirable tonnage openings.
[줄 1106] [93.8%] (30/32) ✅ 유지 - Further changes to tonnage requirements in 1969 led to the universal system of tonnage measurement without the need for tonnage marks, although older ships did retain their original tonnages up until 1994.
[줄 1107] [100.0%] (10/10) ✅ 유지 - Originally the machinery position was amidships with paddle wheel propulsion.
[줄 1108] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Also, with coal being burnt as the propulsive fuel, bunkers were then favorably placed amidships for trim purposes.
[줄 1109] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - With the use of oil fuel this problem was more or less overcome, and with screw propulsion there are definite advantages in having the machinery aft.
[줄 1110] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Taking the machinery right aft can produce an excessive trim by the stern in the light condition and the vessel is then provided with deep tanks forward.
[줄 1111] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - This may lead to a large bending moment in the ballast condition, and a compromise is often reached by placing the machinery three-quarters aft.
[줄 1112] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - That is, there are say three or four holds forward and one aft of the machinery space.
[줄 1113] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In either arrangement the amidships portion with its better stowage shape is reserved for cargo, and shaft spaces lost to cargo are reduced.
[줄 1114] [92.3%] (24/26) ✅ 유지 - The all-aft cargo ship illustrating the final evolution of the dry cargo ship in Figure 3.2 could represent the sophisticated cargo liners of the
[줄 1115] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - a continuous ground bar with the butt welds in the shell plating, ground bar, and bilge keel staggered.
[줄 1116] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Direct connection between the ground bar butt welds and the bilge plate and bilge keel butt welds and the ground bar are avoided.
[줄 1117] [81.8%] (18/22) ✅ 유지 - In ships over 65 m in length, holes are drilled in the bilge keel butt welds as shown in Figure 17.5.
[줄 1118] [96.9%] (31/32) ✅ 유지 - The ground bar thickness is at least that of the bilge plate or 14 mm, whichever is the lesser, and the material grade is the same as that of the bilge plate.
[줄 1119] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Connection of the ground bar to the shell is by continuous fillet welds and the bilge keel is connected to the ground bar by light continuous or staggered intermittent weld.
[줄 1120] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The latter lighter weld ensures that should the bilge keel be fouled, failure occurs at this joint without the bilge plate being damaged.
[줄 1121] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Bilge keels are gradually tapered at their ends and finish in way of an internal stiffening member.
