[줄 1143] [75.6%] (59/78) ✅ 유지 - 18 Bulkheads and pillars Chapter Outline Bulkheads 207 Spacing of watertight bulkheads cargo ships 208 Spacing of watertight bulkheads passenger ships 209 Construction of watertight bulkheads 209 Testing watertight bulkheads 213 Watertight doors 213 Deep tanks 214 Construction of deep tanks 216 Testing deep tanks 216 Topside tanks 218 Shaft tunnel 218 Construction of the shaft tunnel 218 Pillars 220 Spacing of hold pillars 220 Pillar construction 220 Small pillars 223 Further reading 223 Some useful websites 223
[줄 1144] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - This chapter deals with the internal vertical structure of the ship.
[줄 1145] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Much of this structure, particularly the pillars and to some extent the transverse strength bulkheads, is responsible for carrying the vertical loading experienced by the ship.
[줄 1146] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - The principal bulkheads subdivide the ship hull into a number of large watertight compartments, and their construction and spacing is discussed.
[줄 1147] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Also considered are the boundaries of other smaller compartments, such as deep tanks and the shaft tunnel.
[줄 1148] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Bulkheads Vertical partitions in a ship arranged transversely or fore and aft are referred to as 'bulkheads'.
[줄 1149] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Those bulkheads that are of greatest importance are the main hull transverse and longitudinal bulkheads, dividing the ship into a number of watertight compartments.
[줄 1150] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Other lighter bulkheads, named 'minor bulkheads', which act as screens further subdividing compartments into small units of accommodation or stores, are of little structural importance.
[줄 1151] [100.0%] (3/3) ✅ 유지 - All rights reserved.
[줄 1152] [97.1%] (33/34) ✅ 유지 - The main hull bulkheads of sufficient strength are made watertight in order that they may contain any flooding in the event of a compartment on one side of the bulkhead being bilged or breached.
[줄 1153] [96.6%] (28/29) ✅ 유지 - Further, they serve as a hull strength member, not only carrying some of the ship's vertical loading but also resisting any tendency for transverse deformation of the ship.
[줄 1154] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - As a rule the strength of the transverse watertight bulkheads is maintained to the strength deck, which may be above the freeboard deck.
[줄 1155] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Finally, each of the main hull bulkheads has often proved a very effective barrier to the spread of a hold or machinery space fire.
[줄 1156] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Spacing of watertight bulkheads cargo ships The minimum number of transverse watertight bulkheads that must be fitted in a dry cargo ship are stipulated.
[줄 1157] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - A collision bulkhead must be fitted forward, an aft peak bulkhead must be fitted, and watertight bulkheads must be provided at either end of the machinery space.
[줄 1158] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - This implies that for a vessel with machinery amidships the minimum possible number of watertight bulkheads is four.
[줄 1159] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - With the machinery aft this minimum number may be reduced to three, the aft peak bulkhead being at the aft end of the machinery space.
[줄 1160] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Of these bulkheads, perhaps the most important is the collision bulkhead forward.
[줄 1161] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - It is a fact that the bow of at least one out of two ships involved in a collision will be damaged.
[줄 1162] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - For this reason a heavy bulkhead is specified and located so that it is not so far forward as to be damaged on impact.
[줄 1163] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Neither should it be too far aft so that the compartment flooded forward causes excessive trim by the bow.
[줄 1164] [86.5%] (32/37) ✅ 유지 - Classification societies require the location for ships whose length does not exceed 200 m as not less than 5% and not greater than 8% of the ship's length from the fore end of the load waterline.
[줄 1165] [94.1%] (16/17) ✅ 유지 - A minimum distance of 10 meters may also be specified to ensure that the bulkhead is effective.
[줄 1166] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - As a rule this bulkhead is fitted at the minimum distance in order to gain the maximum length for cargo stowage.
[줄 1167] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - The aft peak bulkhead is intended to enclose the stern tubes in a watertight compartment, preventing any emergency from leakage where the propeller shafts pierce the hull.
[줄 1168] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - It is located well aft so that the peak when flooded would not cause excessive trim by the stern.
[줄 1169] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - Machinery bulkheads provide a selfcontained compartment for engines and boilers, preventing damage to these vital components of the ship by flooding in an adjacent hold.
[줄 1170] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - They also localize any fire originating in these spaces.
[줄 1171] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - A minimum number of watertight bulkheads will only be found in smaller cargo ships.
[줄 1172] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - As the size increases the classification society will recommend additional bulkheads, partly to provide greater transverse strength, and also to increase the amount of subdivision.
[줄 1173] [83.3%] (15/18) ✅ 유지 - Table 18.1 indicates the number of watertight bulkheads recommended by Lloyd's Register for any cargo ship.
[줄 1174] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - These should be spaced at uniform intervals, but the shipowner may require for a certain trade a longer hold, which is permitted if additional approved transverse stiffening is provided.
[줄 1175] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - It is possible to dispense with one watertight bulkhead altogether, with Lloyd's Register approval, if adequate approved structural compensation is introduced.
[줄 1176] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - In container ships the spacing is arranged to suit the standard length of containers carried.
[줄 1177] [97.7%] (42/43) ✅ 유지 - By the mid 1970s many of the cargo liner trades had been taken over by the container ship and much of the short haul trade undertaken by the conventional dry cargo ship had passed to the 'roll-on roll-off' type of vessel.
[줄 1178] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - Container ships A feature of the container ship is the stowage of the rectangular container units within the fuller rectangular portion of the hull and their arrangement in tiers above the main deck level.
[줄 1179] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - In order to facilitate removal and placing of the container units of internationally agreed standard dimensions hold and hatch widths are common.
[줄 1180] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The narrow deck width outboard of the hatch opening forms the crown of a double shell space containing wing ballast tanks and passageways.
[줄 1181] [92.9%] (13/14) ✅ 유지 - Later container ship designs feature hatchless vessels that provide a faster turnaround in port.
[줄 1182] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - These may have hatch covers on the forward holds only, or none at all, and are provided with substantial stripping pumps for removing rain and green water from the holds.
[줄 1183] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - In recent years the size of container ships making oceanic voyages has substantially increased.
[줄 1184] [75.0%] (12/16) ✅ 유지 - The largest ships are those operated by Maersk, which can carry a reported 13,500 TEU.
[줄 1185] [87.5%] (21/24) ✅ 유지 - These are unusual and most large ships are between with one classification society reporting more than 60 vessels of at least 8000 TEU classed.
[줄 1186] [94.1%] (16/17) ✅ 유지 - Barge-carrying ships Another development in the cargo liner trade was the introduction of the bargecarrying vessel.
[줄 1187] [100.0%] (40/40) ✅ 유지 - An early version of this type of ship had a particular advantage in maintaining a scheduled service between the ports at mouths of large river systems such as between the Mississippi river in the USA and the Rhine in Europe.
[줄 1188] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - Standard unit cargo barges are carried on board ship and placed overboard or lifted onboard at terminal ports by large deck-mounted gantries or elevator platforms in association with traveling rails.
[줄 1189] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Other designs make provision for floating the barges in and out of the carrying ship, which can be ballasted to accommodate them.
[줄 1190] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - This development appears not to have been as successful as was initially envisaged in the late 1970s, and whilst the merits of this type of craft are still often referred to, the type is now rarely seen.
[줄 1191] [93.9%] (31/33) ✅ 유지 - Ro-ro ships These ships are characterized by the stern and in some cases the bow or side doors giving access to a vehicle deck above the waterline but below the upper deck.
[줄 1192] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Access within the ship may be provided in the form of ramps or lifts leading from this vehicle deck to upper decks or hold below.
[줄 1193] [94.6%] (35/37) ✅ 유지 - Ro-ro ships may be fitted with various patent ramps for loading through the shell doors when not trading to regular ports where link span and other shore-side facilities that are designed to suit are available.
[줄 1194] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Cargo is carried in vehicles and trailers or in unitized form loaded by fork-lift and other trucks.
[줄 1195] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - In order to permit the drive-through vehicle deck
[줄 1196] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - Each of the main watertight hold bulkheads may extend to the uppermost continuous deck, but in the case where the freeboard is measured from the second deck they need only be taken to that deck.
[줄 1197] [100.0%] (38/38) ✅ 유지 - The collision bulkhead extends to the uppermost continuous deck and the aft peak bulkhead may terminate at the first deck above the load waterline provided this is made watertight to the stern, or to a watertight transom floor.
[줄 1198] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - In the case of bulk carriers a further consideration may come into the spacing of the watertight bulkheads where a shipowner desires to obtain a reduced freeboard.
[줄 1199] [93.9%] (31/33) ✅ 유지 - It is possible with bulk carriers to obtain a reduced freeboard under The International Load Line Convention 1966 if it is possible to flood one or more compartments without loss of the vessel.
[줄 1200] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - For obvious reasons many shipowners will wish to obtain the maximum permissible draft for this type of vessel and the bulkhead spacing will be critical.
[줄 1201] [89.5%] (51/57) ✅ 유지 - Additionally, SOLAS amendments now require that bulk carriers constructed after 1 July 1999 and of 150 meters or more in length of singleside skin construction and designed to carry solid bulk cargoes of 1000 kg/cubic meter or more when loaded to the summer load line must be able to withstand flooding of any one cargo hold.
[줄 1202] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - Spacing of watertight bulkheads passenger ships Where a vessel requires a passenger certificate, it is necessary for that vessel to comply with the requirements of the International Convention on Safety of Life at Sea, 1974.
[줄 1203] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Under this convention the subdivision of the passenger ship is strictly specified, and controlled by the authorities of the maritime countries who are signatories to the convention.
[줄 1204] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - In the United Kingdom the controlling authority is the Marine and Coastguard Agency.
[줄 1205] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - Construction of watertight bulkheads The plating of a flat transverse bulkhead is generally welded in horizontal strakes, and convenient two-dimensional units for prefabrication are formed.
[줄 1206] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Smaller bulkheads may be erected as a single unit; larger bulkheads are in two or more units.
[줄 1207] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - always been the practice to use horizontal strakes of plating since the plate thickness increases with depth below the top of the bulkhead.
[줄 1208] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - The reason for this is that the plate thickness is directly related to the pressure exerted by the head of water when a compartment on one side of the bulkhead is flooded.
[줄 1209] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - Apart from the depth, the plate thickness is also influenced by the supporting stiffener spacing.
[줄 1210] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Vertical stiffeners are fitted to the transverse watertight bulkheads of a ship, the span being less in this direction and the stiffener therefore having less tendency to deflect under load.
[줄 1211] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - Stiffening is usually in the form of welded inverted ordinary angle bars, or offset bulb plates, the size of the stiffener being dependent on the unsupported length, stiffener spacing, and rigidity of the end connections.
[줄 1212] [100.0%] (41/41) ✅ 유지 - Rigidity of the end connections will depend on the form of end connection, stiffeners in holds being bracketed or simply directly welded to the tank top or underside of deck, whilst upper tween stiffeners need not have any connection at all.
[줄 1213] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - Vertical stiffeners may be supported by horizontal stringers, permitting a reduction in the stiffener scantling as a result of the reduced span.
[줄 1214] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Horizontal stringers are mostly found on those bulkheads forming the boundaries of a tank space, and in this context are dealt with later.
[줄 1215] [95.7%] (44/46) ✅ 유지 - It is not uncommon to find in present-day ships swedged and corrugated bulkheads, the swedges like the troughs of a corrugated bulkhead being so designed and spaced as to provide sufficient rigidity to the plate bulkhead in order that conventional stiffeners may be dispensed with.
[줄 1216] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - Both swedges and corrugations are arranged in the vertical direction like the stiffeners on transverse and short longitudinal pillar bulkheads.
[줄 1217] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - Since the plating is swedged or corrugated prior to its fabrication, the bulkhead will be plated vertically with a uniform thickness equivalent to that required at the base of the bulkhead.
[줄 1218] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - This implies that the actual plating will be somewhat heavier than that for a conventional bulkhead, and this will to a large extent offset any saving in weight gained by not fitting stiffeners.
[줄 1219] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - At the lower end of transverse hold bulkheads in bulk carriers a bulkhead stool is generally fitted at the lower end of the bulkhead.
[줄 1220] [94.7%] (18/19) ✅ 유지 - This provides a shedder surface for cargo removal rather than a tight corner at the bulkhead/tank top interface.
[줄 1221] [93.3%] (14/15) ✅ 유지 - Inclined shedder plates or gussets are also fitted between the corrugations directly above the stool.
[줄 1222] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - The addition of a vertical plate bracket under the inclined shedder plate at the midpoint of the corrugation stiffens and supports the corrugation against collapse under load.
[줄 1223] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - The boundaries of the bulkhead are double continuously fillet welded directly to the shell, decks, and tank top.
[줄 1224] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - A bulkhead may be erected in thevertical position prior to the fitting of decks during prefabrication on the berth or assembly into a building block.
[줄 1225] [93.9%] (31/33) ✅ 유지 - At the line of the tween decks a 'shelf plate' is fitted to the bulkhead and when erected the tween decks land on this plate, which extends 300–400 mm from the bulkhead.
[줄 1226] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - The deck is lap welded to the shelf plate with an overlap of about 25 mm.
[줄 1227] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In the case of a corrugated bulkhead it becomes necessary to fit filling pieces between the troughs in way of the shelf plate.
[줄 1228] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - If possible the passage of piping and ventilation trunks through watertight bulkheads is avoided.
[줄 1229] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - However, in a number of cases this is impossible and to maintain the integrity of the bulkhead the pipe is flanged at the bulkhead.
[줄 1230] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - Where a ventilation trunk passes through, a watertight shutter is provided.

[줄 1234] [100.0%] (43/43) ✅ 유지 - Testing watertight bulkheads Both the collision bulkhead, as the fore peak bulkhead, and the aft peak bulkhead, provided they do not form the boundaries of tanks, are to be tested by filling the peaks with water to the level of the load waterline.
[줄 1235] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - All bulkheads, unless they form the boundaries of a tank that is regularly subject to a head of liquid, are hose tested.
[줄 1236] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Since it is not considered prudent to test ordinary watertight bulkheads by filling a cargo hold, the hose test is considered satisfactory.
[줄 1237] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Watertight doors In order to maintain the efficiency of a watertight bulkhead it is desirable that it remains intact.
[줄 1238] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - However, in some instances it becomes necessary to provide access between compartments on either side of a watertight bulkhead and watertight doors are fitted for this purpose.
[줄 1239] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - A particular example of this in cargo ships is the direct means of access required between the engine room and the shaft tunnel.
[줄 1240] [80.0%] (20/25) ✅ 유지 - In passenger Shedder plate Plan Corrugated transverse bulkhead Shedder plate Bulkhead stool Transverse floors Bottom shell Tank top Elevation Figure 18.3 Bulk carrierbulkhead stool.
[줄 1241] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - ships watertight doors are more frequently found where they allow passengers to pass between one point of the accommodation and another.
[줄 1242] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Where a doorway is cut in the lower part of a watertight bulkhead care must be taken to maintain the strength of the bulkhead.
[줄 1243] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - The opening is to be framed and reinforced if the vertical stiffeners are cut in way of the opening.
[줄 1244] [94.1%] (32/34) ✅ 유지 - If the stiffener spacing is increased to accommodate the opening, the scantlings of the stiffeners on either side of the opening are increased to give an equivalent strength to that of an unpierced bulkhead.
[줄 1245] [88.5%] (23/26) ✅ 유지 - The actual opening is kept as small as possible, the access to the shaft tunnel being about 1000–1250 mm high and about 700 mm wide.
[줄 1246] [100.0%] (10/10) ✅ 유지 - In passenger accommodation the openings would obviously be somewhat larger.
[줄 1247] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Mild steel or cast steel watertight doors fitted below the waterline are either of the vertical or horizontal sliding type.
[줄 1248] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - A swinging hinged type of door could prove impossible to close in the event of flooding and is not permitted.
[줄 1249] [97.1%] (34/35) ✅ 유지 - The sliding door must be capable of operation when the ship is listed 15 , and be opened or closed from the vicinity of the door as well as from a position above the bulkhead deck.
[줄 1250] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - At this remote control position an indicator must be provided to show whether the door is open or closed.
[줄 1251] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Vertical sliding doors may be closed by a vertical screw thread, which is turned by a shaft extending above the bulkhead and fitted with a crank handle.
[줄 1252] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - This screw thread turns in a gunmetal nut attached to the top of the door, and a crank handle is also provided at the door to allow it to be closed from this position.
[줄 1253] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Often horizontal sliding doors are fitted, and these may have a vertical shaft extending above the bulkhead deck, which may be operated by hand from above the deck or at the door.
[줄 1254] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - This can also be power driven by an electric motor and worm gear, the vertical shaft working through bevel wheels, and horizontal screwed shafts turning in bronze nuts on the door.
[줄 1255] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - The horizontal sliding door may also be opened and closed by a hydraulic ram with a hydraulic hand pump and with control at the door and above the bulkhead deck.
[줄 1256] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - With the larger number of watertight doors fitted in passenger ships the doors may be closed by means of hydraulic power actuated by remote control from a central position above the bulkhead deck.
[줄 1257] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - When in place all watertight doors are given a hose test, but those in a passenger ship are required to be tested under a head of water extending to the bulkhead deck.
[줄 1258] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - This may be done before the door is fitted in the ship.
[줄 1259] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - In approved positions in the upper tween decks well above the waterline, hinged watertight doors are permitted.
[줄 1260] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - These may be similar to the weathertight doors fitted in superstructures, but are to have gunmetal pins in the hinges.

[줄 1268] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Most ships now have their machinery arranged aft or occasionally three-quarters aft, and are fitted with deep tanks forward to improve the trim in the light conditions.
[줄 1269] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Construction of deep tanks Bulkheads that form the boundaries of a deep tank differ from hold bulkheads in that they are regularly subjected to pressure from a head of liquid.
[줄 1270] [100.0%] (50/50) ✅ 유지 - The conventional hold bulkhead may be allowed to deflect and tolerate high stresses on the rare occasions when it has to withstand temporary flooding of a hold, but deep tank bulkheads, which are regularly loaded in this manner, are required to have greater rigidity and be subject to lower stresses.
[줄 1271] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - As a result the plate and stiffener scantlings will be larger in way of deep tanks, and additional stiffening may be introduced.
[줄 1272] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - The greater plating thickness of the tank boundary bulkheads increases with tank depth, and with increasing stiffener spacing.
[줄 1273] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - To provide the greater rigidity the vertical stiffeners are of heavier scantlings and more closely spaced.
[줄 1274] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - They must be bracketed or welded to some other form of stiffening member at their ends.
[줄 1275] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - Vertical stiffener sizes may be reduced, however, by fitting horizontal girders that form a continuous line of support on the bulkheads and ship's side.
[줄 1276] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - These horizontal girders are connected at their ends by flanged brackets and are supported by tripping brackets at the toes of the end brackets, and at every third stiffener or frame.
[줄 1277] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - Intermediate frames and stiffeners are effectively connected to the horizontal girders.
[줄 1278] [97.7%] (43/44) ✅ 유지 - Where deep tanks are intended to carry oil fuel for the ship's use, or oil cargoes, there will be a free surface, and it is necessary to fit a center-line bulkhead where the tanks extend from side to side of the ship.
[줄 1279] [100.0%] (8/8) ✅ 유지 - This is to reduce the free surface effect.
[줄 1280] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - The center-line bulkhead may be intact or perforated, and where intact the scantlings will be the same as for boundary bulkheads.
[줄 1281] [96.4%] (27/28) ✅ 유지 - If perforated, the area of perforations is sufficient to reduce liquid pressures, and the bulkhead stiffeners have considerably reduced scantlings, surging being avoided by limiting the perforation area.
[줄 1282] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - Both swedged and corrugated plating can be used to advantage in the construction of deep tanks since, without the conventional stiffening, tanks are more easily cleaned.
[줄 1283] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - However, the use of corrugations does cause problems in ship construction.
[줄 1284] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - With conventional welded stiffening it may be convenient to arrange the stiffeners outside the tank so that the boundary bulkhead has a plain inside for ease of cleaning.
[줄 1285] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - In cargo ships where various liquid cargoes are carried, arrangements may be made to fit cofferdams between deep tanks.
[줄 1286] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - As these tanks may also be fitted immediately forward of the machine space, a pipe tunnel is generally fitted through them with access from the engine room.
[줄 1287] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - This tunnel carries the bilge piping as it is undesirable to pass this through the deep tanks carrying oil cargoes.
[줄 1288] [97.0%] (32/33) ✅ 유지 - Testing deep tanks Deep tanks are tested by subjecting them to the maximum head of water to which they might be subject in service i.e to the top of the air pipe.
[줄 1289] [80.0%] (12/15) ✅ 유지 - This should not be less than 2.45 m above the crown of the tank.

[줄 1293] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Topside tanks Standard general bulk carriers are fitted with topside tanks that may be used for water ballast, and in some instances are used for the carriage of light grains.
[줄 1294] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - The thickness of the sloping bulkhead of this tank is determined in a similar manner to that of the deep tank bulkheads.
[줄 1295] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - In present practice, as indicated in Chapter 17, the topside tank is generally stiffened internally by longitudinal framing supported by transverses.
[줄 1296] [100.0%] (39/39) ✅ 유지 - Transverses are arranged in line with the end of the main cargo hatchways, and in large ships a fore and aft diaphragm may be fitted at half the width of the tank, between the deck and the sloping plating.
[줄 1297] [97.4%] (38/39) ✅ 유지 - Shaft tunnel When the ship's machinery is not located fully aft it is necessary to enclose the propeller shaft or shafts in a watertight tunnel between the aft end of the machinery space and the aft peak bulkhead.
[줄 1298] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - This protects the shaft from the cargo and provides a watertight compartment that will contain any flooding resulting from damage to the watertight gland at the aft peak bulkhead.
[줄 1299] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - The tunnel should be large enough to permit access for inspection and repair of the shafting.
[줄 1300] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - A sliding watertight door that may be opened from either side is provided at the forward end in the machinery space bulkhead.
[줄 1301] [100.0%] (42/42) ✅ 유지 - Two means of escape from the shaft tunnel must be provided, and as a rule there is a ladder in a watertight trunk leading to an escape hatch on the deck above the waterline, at the aft end of the shaft tunnel.
[줄 1302] [97.7%] (42/43) ✅ 유지 - Where the ship narrows at its after end the aftermost hold may be completely plated over at the level of the shaft tunnel to form a tunnel flat, as the narrow stowage space either side of the conventional shaft tunnel cannot be utilized.
[줄 1303] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - The additional space under this tunnel flat is often used to stow the spare tail shaft.
[줄 1304] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Shaft tunnels also provide a convenient means of carrying piping aft, which is then accessible and protected from cargo damage.
[줄 1305] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Construction of the shaft tunnel The thickness of the tunnel plating is determined in the same manner as that for the watertight bulkheads.
[줄 1306] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Where the top of the tunnel is well rounded the thickness of the top plating may be reduced, but where the top is flat it is increased.
[줄 1307] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Under hatchways the top plating must be increased in thickness unless it is covered by wood of a specified thickness.
[줄 1308] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - Vertical stiffeners supporting the tunnel plating have similar scantlings to the watertight bulkhead stiffeners and their lower end is welded to the tank top.
[줄 1309] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - On completion the shaft tunnel structure is subject to a hose test.
[줄 1310] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - At intervals along the length of the shaft, stools are built that support the shaft bearings.
[줄 1311] [97.1%] (33/34) ✅ 유지 - A walkway is installed on one side of the shaft to permit inspection and, as a result, in a single screw ship the shaft tunnel will be offset from the ship's center line.
[줄 1312] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - This walkway is formed by gratings laid on angle bearers supported by struts etc.; any piping is then led along underneath the walkway.

[줄 1315] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - The key requirement of a new ship is that it can trade profitably, so economics is of prime importance in designing a merchant ship.
[줄 1316] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - An owner requires a ship that will give the best possible returns for the owner's initial investment and running costs.
[줄 1317] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - The final design should be arrived at taking into account not only present economic considerations, but also those likely to develop within the life of the ship.
[줄 1318] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - This is especially the case for some trades, for example LNG, where the ship is expected to work the same route for its working life.
[줄 1319] [100.0%] (6/6) ✅ 유지 - Design for operation is the result.
[줄 1320] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - For other ships, including bulk carriers, the first cost of the ship is the major factor for the owner and the ship may be designed for ease of production.
[줄 1321] [100.0%] (13/13) ✅ 유지 - Resale value is also often a major consideration, leading to design for maintenance.
[줄 1322] [100.0%] (41/41) ✅ 유지 - With the aid of computers it is possible to make a study of a large number of varying design parameters and to arrive at a ship design that is not only technically feasible but, more importantly, is the most economically efficient.
[줄 1323] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - Ideally the design will take into consideration first cost, operating cost, and future maintenance.
[줄 1324] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Preparation of the design The initial design of a ship generally proceeds through three stages: concept; preliminary; and contract design.
[줄 1325] [100.0%] (38/38) ✅ 유지 - The process of initial design is often illustrated by the design spiral, which indicates that given the objectives of the design, the designer works towards the best solution adjusting and balancing the interrelated parameters as the designer goes.
[줄 1326] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - A concept design should, from the objectives, provide sufficient information for a basic techno-economic assessment of the alternatives to be made.
[줄 1327] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Economic criteria that may be derived for commercial ship designs and used to measure their profitability are net present value, discounted cash flow, or required freight rate.

[줄 1333] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - Pillars The prime function of the pillars is to carry the load of the decks and weights upon the decks vertically down to the ship's bottom structure where these loads are supported by the upward buoyant forces.
[줄 1334] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - A secondary function of pillars is to tie together the structure in a vertical direction.
[줄 1335] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - Within the main hull of a cargo ship two different forms of pillar may be found, those in the holds invariably fulfilling the first function and those in the machinery spaces fulfilling the latter function.
[줄 1336] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Hold pillars, primarily in compression, are often without bracket connections at their ends, whilst machinery space pillars are heavily bracketed at their ends to permit tensile loadings.
[줄 1337] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - This latter type of pillar may also be found in tank spaces where the crown of tank under pressure can put the pillar in tension.
[줄 1338] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Spacing of hold pillars Since pillars located in holds will interfere with the stowage arrangements, widely spaced pillars of large fabricated section are used rather than small, solid, closely spaced pillar systems.
[줄 1339] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - The arrangement most often found in cargo ships is a two-row pillar system, with pillars at the hatch corners or mid-length of hatch supporting deck girders adjacent to the hatch sides.
[줄 1340] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - As the deck girder size is to some extent dependent on the supported span, where only a mid-hatch length pillar is fitted the girder scantlings will be greater than that where two hatch corner pillars are fitted.
[줄 1341] [100.0%] (39/39) ✅ 유지 - In fact, pillars may be eliminated altogether where it is important that a clear space should be provided, but the deck girder will then be considerably larger, and may be supported at its ends by webs at the bulkhead.
[줄 1342] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Substantial transverse cantilevers may also be fitted to support the side decks.
[줄 1343] [97.0%] (32/33) ✅ 유지 - Pillars may also be fitted in holds on the ship's center line at the hatch end, to support the heavy hatch end beams securely connected to and supporting the hatch side girders.
[줄 1344] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - In a similar position it is not unusual to find short corrugated fore and aft pillar bulkheads.
[줄 1345] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - These run from the forward or aft side of the hatch opening to the adjacent transverse bulkhead on the ship's center line.
[줄 1346] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - To maintain continuity of loading the tween pillars are arranged directly above the hold pillars.
[줄 1347] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - If this is not possible stiffening arrangements should be made to carry the load from the tween pillar to the hold pillar below.
[줄 1348] [100.0%] (45/45) ✅ 유지 - Pillar construction It has already been seen that the hold pillar is primarily subject to a compressive loading, and if buckling is to be avoided in service the required cross-section must be designed with both the load carried and length of pillar in mind.
[줄 1349] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - The ideal section for a compressive strut is the tubular section and this is often adopted for hold pillars, hollow rectangular and octagonal sections also being used.
[줄 1350] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - For economic reasons the sections are fabricated in lengths from steel plate, and for the hollow rectangular section welded channels or angles may also be used.
[줄 1351] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - A small flat bar or cope bar may be tack welded inside these pillar sections to allow them to be welded externally.
[줄 1352] [93.2%] (110/118) ✅ 유지 - Weld Tubular pillar PILLAR SECTIONS Weld Hollow square pillar Weld Weld into backing bar Backing bar Weld Hollow square pillar Octagonal pillar Weld Weld Formed by flanged plates Formed by two angles or flanged plates Weld Hatch coaming Plate bracket Heavy rider plate Deck Hatch coaming Deck Plate bracket Pillar Pillar Half beam Heavy rider plate Half beam Deck Girder at hatch side Pillar Deck girder Tripping brackets Deck Heavy plate introduced into deck girder flange in way of pillar Bracket Pillar Bracket Half beam HEAD DETAILS ENGINE ROOM PILLAR PILLAR SECTION Pillar Bracket Insert plate in tank top Intercostal side girder Intercostal side girder Tank top Pillar HEEL DETAILS Solid floor Solid floor Figure 18.7 Pillars.

[줄 1355] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Pillars have a bearing fit, and it is important that the loads at the head and heel of the pillar should be well distributed.
[줄 1356] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - At the head of the pillar a continuous weld is made to a doubling plate supported by brackets.
[줄 1357] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Details of the head fitting vary from ship to ship and depend very much on the form of hatch side or deck girder that they support.
[줄 1358] [100.0%] (42/42) ✅ 유지 - The heel of the hold pillar lands on a heavy doubling or insert plate at the tank top and it is commonly arranged that the point of loading will coincide with a solid floor/side girder intersection in the double bottom below.
[줄 1359] [94.7%] (18/19) ✅ 유지 - Where this is not possible partial floors and short intercostal side girders may be fitted to distribute the load.
[줄 1360] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Machinery space pillars are fabricated from angles, channels, or rolled steel joists, and are heavily bracketed to suitably stiffened members.
[줄 1361] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - Small pillars Within the accommodation and in relatively small vessels, solid round steel pillars having diameters seldom exceeding 150 mm may be fitted.
[줄 1362] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - These may have forged palms at their head and heel, the head being welded to a continuous angle fore and aft runner that supports the deck.
[줄 1363] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Alternatively, the pillar head may have a direct continuous weld connection to an inverted angle beam or deck girder, with suitable tripping brackets fitted directly above.
[줄 1364] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - The heel is then directly welded to the deck, which is suitably stiffened below.
[줄 1365] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Rolled hollow steel section pillars of similar size with direct welded head and heel fittings are commonly used today in lieu of small solid pillars.

[줄 1371] [78.3%] (47/60) ✅ 유지 - Hatch covers 232 Bulwarks 235 Construction of bulwarks 235 Superstructures and deckhouses 237 Forecastle 237 Bridge structures 238 Poop structure 238 Passenger ship superstructures 238 Weathertight doors 240 Further reading 240 Some useful websites 240 Decks at different levels in a ship serve various functions; they may be either watertight decks, strength decks, or simply cargo and passenger accommodation decks.
[줄 1372] [97.5%] (39/40) ✅ 유지 - Watertight decks are fitted to maintain the integrity of the main watertight hull, and the most important is the freeboard deck, which is the uppermost deck having permanent means of closing all openings in the exposed portions of that deck.
[줄 1373] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - Although all decks contribute to some extent to the strength of the ship, the most important is that which forms the upper flange of the main hull girder, called the 'strength deck'.
[줄 1374] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - Lighter decks that are not watertight may be fitted to provide platforms for passenger accommodation and permit more flexible cargo-loading arrangements.
[줄 1375] [96.9%] (31/32) ✅ 유지 - In general cargo ships these lighter decks form tweens that provide spaces in which goods may be stowed without their being crushed by a large amount of other cargo stowed above them.
[줄 1376] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - To permit loading and discharging of cargo, openings must be cut in the decks, and these may be closed by nonwatertight or watertight hatches.
[줄 1377] [100.0%] (39/39) ✅ 유지 - Other openings are required for personal access through the decks, and in way of the machinery space casing openings are provided that allow the removal of machinery items when necessary, and also provide light and air to this space.

[줄 1381] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Forward and aft on the uppermost continuous deck a forecastle and often a poop may be provided to protect the ends of the ship at sea.
[줄 1382] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - The weather decks of ships are cambered to facilitate the draining of water from the decks in heavy weather.
[줄 1383] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - The camber may be parabolic or straight,the latter being preferred in many cases to allow panel lines to be used for the production of the deck panels.
[줄 1384] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - There may be advantages in fitting horizontal decks in some ships, particularly if containers are carried and regular cross-sections are desired.
[줄 1385] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Short lengths of internal deck or flats are as a rule horizontal.
[줄 1386] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - Decks are arranged in plate panels with transverse or longitudinal stiffening, and local stiffening in way of any openings.
[줄 1387] [100.0%] (14/14) ✅ 유지 - Longitudinal deck girders may support the transverse framing, and deep transverses the longitudinal framing.
[줄 1388] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Deck plating The heaviest deck plating will be found abreast the hatch openings of the strength deck.
[줄 1389] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Plating that lies within the line of the hatch openings contributes little to the longitudinal strength of the deck and it is therefore appreciably lighter.
[줄 1390] [94.9%] (37/39) ✅ 유지 - As the greatest longitudinal bending stresses will occur over the midship region, the greatest deck plate thickness is maintained over 40% of the length amidships, and it tapers to a minimum thickness permitted at the ends of the ship.
[줄 1391] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - Locally, the plating thickness may be increased where higher stresses occur owing to discontinuities in the structure or concentrated loads.
[줄 1392] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Other thickness increases may occur where large deck loads are carried, where fork-lift trucks or other wheeled vehicles are to be used, and in way of deep tanks.
[줄 1393] [90.9%] (40/44) ✅ 유지 - Where the strength deck plating exceeds 30 mm it is to be Grade B steel and if it exceeds 40 mm Grade D over the midships region, at the ends of the superstructure, and in way of the cargo hold region in container ships.
[줄 1394] [79.7%] (51/64) ✅ 유지 - The stringer plate i.e the strake of deck plating adjacent to the sheerstrake of the strength deck, over the midship region and container ship cargo hold area, of ships less than 260 meters in length, is to be of Grade B steel if 15–20 mm thick, Grade D if 20–25 mm thick, and Grade E if more than 25 mm thick.
[줄 1395] [80.8%] (21/26) ✅ 유지 - Where the steel deck temperatures fall below 0  C in refrigerated cargo ships the steel will be of Grades B, D, and E depending on thickness.
[줄 1396] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - On decks other than the strength deck, the variation in plate thickness is similar, but lighter scantlings are in use.

[줄 1406] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Deck stiffening Decks may be framed transversely or longitudinally, but outside the line of openings it is preferred that longitudinal framing should be adopted for the strength deck.
[줄 1407] [94.6%] (35/37) ✅ 유지 - When the decks are longitudinally framed the scantlings of the longitudinals are dependent on their spacing, the length of ship, whether they are inside or outside the line of hatch openings, their span, and the deck loading.
[줄 1408] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Deck transverses support the longitudinals, and these are built from a deep web plate with flange or welded face flat, and are bracketed to the side frame.
[줄 1409] [91.1%] (41/45) ✅ 유지 - Within the forward 7.5% of the ship's length, the forecastle and weather deck transverses are closely spaced and the longitudinal scantlings increased, the additional transverse and longitudinal stiffening forward being designed to avoid buckling of the deck plating on impact when shipping seas.
[줄 1410] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Transversely framed decks are fitted with deck beams at every frame, and these have scantlings that are dependent on their span, spacing, and location in the ship.
[줄 1411] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - Those fitted right forward on weather decks, like the longitudinal framing forward, have heavier scantlings, and the frame spacing is also decreased in this region so they will be closer together.
[줄 1412] [97.1%] (33/34) ✅ 유지 - Beams fitted in way of deep tanks, peak tanks, and oil bunkers may also have increased scantlings as they are required to have the same rigidity as the stiffeners of the tank boundary bulkheads.
[줄 1413] [95.0%] (19/20) ✅ 유지 - Deck beams are supported by longitudinal deck girders that have similar scantlings to deck transverses fitted with any longitudinal framing.
[줄 1414] [87.0%] (20/23) ✅ 유지 - Within the forward 7.5% of the ship's length these deck girders are more closely spaced on the forecastle and weather decks.
[줄 1415] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Elsewhere the spacing is arranged to suit the deck loads carried and the pillar arrangements adopted.
[줄 1416] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Each beam is connected to the frame by a 'beam knee' and abreast the hatches 'half beams' are fitted with a suitable supporting connection at the hatch side girder.
[줄 1417] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - Both longitudinals and deck beam scantlings are increased in way of cargo decks where fork-lift trucks and other wheeled vehicles, which cause large point loads, are used.
[줄 1418] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - In way of the hatches fore and aft side girders are fitted to support the inboard ends of the half beams and transverses.
[줄 1419] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - At the ends of the hatches heavy transverse beams are fitted and these may be connected at the intersection with the hatch side girder by horizontal gusset plates.
[줄 1420] [90.9%] (20/22) ✅ 유지 - Where the deck plating extends inside the coamings of hatches amidships the side coaming is extended in the form of tapered brackets.

[줄 1429] [93.5%] (29/31) ✅ 유지 - Hull form Between the 1940s and 1970 there was a steady increase in the speed of the dry cargo ship and this was reflected in the hull form of the vessels.

[줄 1434] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - Cargo handling equipment Cargo handling equipment, which remained relatively unchanged for a long period, has received considerable attention since the 1960s.
[줄 1435] [96.6%] (28/29) ✅ 유지 - This was primarily brought about by an awareness of the loss of revenue caused by the long periods of time thevessel may spend in port discharging and loading cargoes.
[줄 1436] [97.2%] (35/36) ✅ 유지 - Conventional cargo ships are now fitted with steel folding and/or rolling steel hatch covers of one patent type or another or liftable slab covers of steel, which reduce maintenance as well as speed cargo handling.
[줄 1437] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Various new lifting devices, derrick forms, and winches have been designed and introduced with marine shipborne cranes now almost completely replacing rigged derrick installations on modern ships.
[줄 1438] [100.0%] (9/9) ✅ 유지 - These provide further increased rates of loading and discharge.

[줄 1451] [88.2%] (15/17) ✅ 유지 - Hatch coamings Heights of coamings and cover closing arrangements in some instances depend on the hatch position.
[줄 1452] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - The positions differentiate between regions that are more exposed than others.
[줄 1453] [85.2%] (23/27) ✅ 유지 - Position 1 indicates that the hatch is on the exposed freeboard deck, raised quarter deck, or superstructure decks within 25% of the ship's length from forward.
[줄 1454] [85.7%] (18/21) ✅ 유지 - Position 2 indicates that the hatch is located on exposed superstructure decks abaft the forward 25% of the ship's length.
[줄 1455] [81.8%] (27/33) ✅ 유지 - Hatches that are at Position 1 have coamings at least 600 mm high and those at Position 2 have coamings at least 450 mm high, the height being measured above any deck covering.
[줄 1456] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - Provision is made for lowering these heights or omitting the coaming altogether if directly secured steel covers are fitted and it can be shown that the safety of the ship would not be impaired in any sea condition.
[줄 1457] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - Where the coaming height is 600 mm or more the upper edge is stiffened by a horizontal bulb flat and supporting stays to the deck are fitted.
[줄 1458] [88.9%] (16/18) ✅ 유지 - Coamings less than 600 mm high are stiffened by a cope or similar bar at their upper edge.
[줄 1459] [90.5%] (19/21) ✅ 유지 - The steel coamings extend down to the lower edge of the deck beams, which are then effectively attached to the coamings.

[줄 1493] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Bulwarks Bulwarks fitted on weather decks are provided as protection for personnel and are not intended as a major structural feature.
[줄 1494] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - They are therefore of light scantlings, and their connections to the adjacent structures are of some importance if high stresses in the bulkwarks are to be avoided.
[줄 1495] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Freeing ports are cut in bulwarks, forming wells on decks in order that water may quickly drain away.
[줄 1496] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - The required area of freeing ports is in accordance with the Load Line Convention requirement.
[줄 1497] [91.2%] (31/34) ✅ 유지 - Construction of bulwarks Bulwarks should be at least 1 m high on the exposed freeboard and superstructure decks, but a reduced height may be permitted if this interferes with the working of the ship.

[줄 1506] [88.5%] (23/26) ✅ 유지 - Superstructures and deckhouses Superstructures may be defined as those erections above the freeboard deck that extend to the ship's side or almost to the side.
[줄 1507] [88.2%] (15/17) ✅ 유지 - Deckhouses are those erections on deck that are well within the line of the ship's side.
[줄 1508] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - Both structures are of importance in the assignment of the load line as they provide protection for the openings through the freeboard deck.
[줄 1509] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Of particular importance in this respect are the end bulkheads of the superstructures, particularly the bridge front, which is to withstand the force of any seas shipped.
[줄 1510] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - The bridge structure amidships or the poop aft are, in accordance with statutory regulations, provided as protection for the machinery openings.
[줄 1511] [97.4%] (37/38) ✅ 유지 - It is possible, however, to dispense with these houses or superstructures and increase considerably the scantlings of the exposed machinery casing, but in other than very small vessels it is unlikely that such an arrangement would be adopted.
[줄 1512] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Unless an excessive sheer is provided on the uppermost deck it is necessary to fit a forecastle forward to give added protection in a seaway.
[줄 1513] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Each structure is utilized to the full, the after structure carrying virtually all the accommodation in modern ships.
[줄 1514] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - The crew may be located all aft in the poop structure or partly housed in any bridge structure with the navigating spaces.
[줄 1515] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Passenger liners have considerable areas of superstructures covering tiers of decks and these will house the majority of passengers and some of the crew.
[줄 1516] [94.4%] (17/18) ✅ 유지 - Of great structural importance is the strength of the vessel where superstructures and deckhouses terminate and are noncontinuous.
[줄 1517] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - At these discontinuities, discussed in Chapter 8, large stresses may arise and additional strengthening will be required locally as indicated in the following notes on the construction.
[줄 1518] [88.9%] (40/45) ✅ 유지 - Long superstructures exceeding 15% of the ship's length and extending within 50% of the vessel's length amidships receive special consideration as they contribute to the longitudinal strength of the ship, and as such must have scantlings consistent with the main hull strength members.
[줄 1519] [95.2%] (40/42) ✅ 유지 - Forecastle Sea-going ships must be fitted with a forecastle that extends at least 7% of the ship's length aft of the stem, and a minimum height of the bow at the forecastle deck above the summer load line is stipulated.
[줄 1520] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - By increasing the upper deck sheer at the forward end to obtain the same height of bow, the forecastle might be dispensed with, but in practice this construction is seldom found.
[줄 1521] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - The side and end plating of the forecastle has a thickness that is dependent on the ship's length and the frame and stiffener spacing adopted, the side plating being somewhat heavier than the aft end plating.
[줄 1522] [91.7%] (22/24) ✅ 유지 - If a long forecastle is fitted such that its end bulkhead comes within 50% of the ship's length amidships, additional stiffening is required.
[줄 1523] [90.0%] (36/40) ✅ 유지 - Bridge structures The side of bridge superstructures whose length exceeds 15% of the ship's length will have a greater thickness than the sides of other houses, the scantling being similar to that required for the ship's side shell.
[줄 1524] [92.3%] (24/26) ✅ 유지 - All bridge superstructures and midship deckhouses will have a heavily plated bridge front, and the aft end plating will be lighter than the front and sides.
[줄 1525] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - Likewise the stiffening members fitted at the forward end will have greater scantlings than those at the sides and aft end.
[줄 1526] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Additional stiffening in the form of web frames or partial bulkheads will be found where there are large erections above the bridge deck.
[줄 1527] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - These are intended to support the sides and ends of the houses above and are preferably arranged over the watertight bulkheads below.
[줄 1528] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Under concentrated loads on the superstructure decks, for example under lifeboat davits, web frames are also provided.
[줄 1529] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - The longer bridge superstructure that is transmitting the main hull girder stresses requires considerable strengthening at the ends.
[줄 1530] [85.2%] (23/27) ✅ 유지 - At this major discontinuity, the upper deck sheerstrake thickness is increased by 20%, the upper deck stringer plate by 20%, and the bridge side plating by 25%.
[줄 1531] [83.8%] (31/37) ✅ 유지 - The latter plating is tapered into the upper deck sheerstrake with a generous radius, as shown in Figure 19.8 a, stiffened at its upper edge, and supported by webs not more than 1.5 m apart.
[줄 1532] [91.9%] (34/37) ✅ 유지 - At the ends of short bridge superstructures less strengthening is required, but local stresses may still be high and therefore the upper deck sheerstrake thickness is still increased by 20% and the upper deck stringer by 20%.
[줄 1533] [89.7%] (26/29) ✅ 유지 - Poop structure Where there is no midship deckhouse or bridge superstructure the poop front will be heavily constructed, its scantlings being similar to those required for a bridge front.
[줄 1534] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - In other ships it is relatively exposed and therefore needs adequate strengthening in all cases.
[줄 1535] [89.5%] (34/38) ✅ 유지 - If the poop front comes within 50% of the ship's length amidships, the discontinuity formed in the main hull girder is to be considerably strengthened, as for a long bridge exceeding 15% of the ship's length.
[줄 1536] [96.2%] (25/26) ✅ 유지 - Where deckhouses are built above the poop deck these are supported by webs or short transverse bulkheads in the same manner as those houses fitted amidships.
[줄 1537] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - The after end of any poop house will have increased scantlings since it is more exposed than other aft end house bulkheads.
[줄 1538] [97.2%] (35/36) ✅ 유지 - Passenger ship superstructures It is shown in Chapter 8 that with conventional beam theory the bending stress distribution is linear, increasing from zero at the neutral axis to a maximum at the upper deck and bottom.
[줄 1539] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - If a long superstructure is fitted the stress distribution remains linear and the strength deck is above the upper deck in way of the superstructure deck.
[줄 1540] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - If a short superstructure is fitted the stress distribution will be broken at the upper deck, which is the strength deck, the stresses in the superstructure deck being less than those in the upper deck.
[줄 1541] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - The long superstructure is referred to as an 'effective superstructure', the erections contributing to the overall strength of the hull girder, and therefore they are substantially built.

[줄 1568] [94.4%] (17/18) ✅ 유지 - In passenger ships with large superstructures the present practice is to make the structure effective with adequate scantlings.
[줄 1569] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - Some older ships have been fitted with expansion joints that are in effect transverse cuts introduced to relieve the hull bending stresses in the houses.
[줄 1570] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - It has been shown that at the end of deck erections the stresses do not conform to beam theory and the ends are ineffective in contributing to the longitudinal strength.
[줄 1571] [96.0%] (24/25) ✅ 유지 - The expansion joints were therefore so arranged that this 'end effect' extended from joint to joint, and lighter scantlings were then permitted for the superstructure.
[줄 1572] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - Unfortunately the expansion joint often provided an ideal 'notch' in the structure from which cracks initiated.
[줄 1573] [100.0%] (42/42) ✅ 유지 - Aluminum alloy superstructures offer an alternative to the use of expansion joints, since the low modulus of elasticity of the material results in lower stresses in the houses than would be the case with a steel superstructure, all other considerations being equal.
[줄 1574] [90.9%] (20/22) ✅ 유지 - Weathertight doors The integrity of houses on the freeboard and other decks that protect the openings in these decks must be maintained.
[줄 1575] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - Access openings must be provided to the houses and weathertight doors are fitted to these openings.
[줄 1576] [100.0%] (25/25) ✅ 유지 - These must comply with the requirements of the Load Line Convention and are steel doors that may be secured and made watertight from either side.
[줄 1577] [92.3%] (12/13) ✅ 유지 - Weathertightness is maintained by a rubber gasket at the frame of the door.

[줄 1590] [97.5%] (39/40) ✅ 유지 - Stem On many conventional ships a stem bar, which is a solid round bar, is fitted from the keel to the waterline region, and a radiused plate is fitted above the waterline to form the upper part of the stem.
[줄 1591] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - This forms what is referred to as a 'soft nose' stem, which in the event of a collision will buckle under load, keeping the impact damage to a minimum.
[줄 1592] [100.0%] (31/31) ✅ 유지 - Older ships had solid bar stems that were riveted and of square section, and as the stem had no rake it could cause considerable damage on impact because of its rigidity.
[줄 1593] [100.0%] (40/40) ✅ 유지 - Small ships such as tugs and trawlers may still have a solid stem bar extending to the top of the bow, and some existing large passenger ships may have steel castings or forgings forming the lower part of the stem.

[줄 1617] [93.3%] (28/30) ✅ 유지 - Chain locker A chain locker is often arranged in the position forward of the collision bulkhead shown in Figure 20.1, below either the main deck or the second deck.

[줄 1619] [100.0%] (40/40) ✅ 유지 - Chain locker dimensions are determined in relation to the length and size of cable, the depth being such that the cable is easily stowed, and a direct lead at all times is provided to the mouth of the chain pipe.
[줄 1620] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - Port and starboard cables are stowed separately in the locker, and the inboard ends of each are secured to the bottom of the center-line bulkhead or underside of deck.

[줄 1622] [100.0%] (37/37) ✅ 유지 - The locker does not as a rule have the same breadth as the ship, but has conventionally stiffened forward and side bulkheads, the stiffeners being conveniently arranged outside the locker if possible to prevent their being damaged.

[줄 1624] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - Where fitted this provides a mudbox that can be cleaned and is drained by a center-line suction, the bottom plating sloping inboard.
[줄 1625] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - To separate the locker into port and starboard compartments a center-line bulkhead is fitted.
[줄 1626] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - This bulkhead does not extend to the crown of the locker, but allows working space above the two compartments.
[줄 1627] [100.0%] (33/33) ✅ 유지 - Access to the bottom of the locker is provided by means of foot holes cut in the bulkhead, and the stiffeners fitted to this bulkhead are of the vertical flush cope bar type.

[줄 1639] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - Hawse pipes To provide an easy lead for the cable from the windlass to the anchors, the hawse pipes must be carefully fitted.

[줄 1646] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Bow thrust units For maneuvering in confined waters at low speeds, lateral bow thrust units are particularly useful.
[줄 1647] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - These are often found in research vessels, or drilling platform vessels where very accurate positioning must be maintained.
[줄 1648] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - They are also to be found in large ships and cross-channel vessels where they are provided as an aid to docking.
[줄 1649] [94.7%] (18/19) ✅ 유지 - The thrust unit consists as a rule of controllable pitch or reversible impeller fitted in an athwartships watertight tunnel.
[줄 1650] [100.0%] (18/18) ✅ 유지 - Control of the unit is from the bridge, but the driving motor is in way of the impeller.
[줄 1651] [96.7%] (29/30) ✅ 유지 - Thrust provided by the impellers is low; 16 tonnes is perhaps the largest fitted, but the unit size does not need to be large as small thrusts are very effective.
[줄 1652] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - It is true, however, that the greatest thrust is provided at zero speed and as the vessel gets under way the unit becomes much less effective.
[줄 1653] [96.4%] (27/28) ✅ 유지 - From a construction point of view the most important feature is the provision of fairing sections at the ends of the athwartship tunnel in way of the shell.
[줄 1654] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - It has been shown that an appreciable increase in hull resistance and hence power may result if this detail is neglected.
[줄 1655] [100.0%] (20/20) ✅ 유지 - The best way of avoiding this is to close the tunnels at either end when they are not in use.
[줄 1656] [100.0%] (15/15) ✅ 유지 - This is possible, flush-mounted, butterfly action, hydraulically operated doors being available for this purpose.
[줄 1657] [86.7%] (13/15) ✅ 유지 - Some useful websites www.brunvoll.no For details of tunnel and azimuth bow thrust units.

[줄 1683] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Stern frame It has already been indicated that the form of the stern frame is influenced by the stern profile and rudder type.
[줄 1684] [100.0%] (30/30) ✅ 유지 - To prevent serious vibration at the after end there must be adequate clearances between the propeller and stern frame, and this will to a large extent dictate its overall size.
[줄 1685] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - The stern frame of a ship may be cast, forged, or fabricated from steel plate and sections.
[줄 1686] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - On larger ships it is generally either cast or fabricated, the casting being undertaken by a specialist works outside the shipyard.
[줄 1687] [100.0%] (32/32) ✅ 유지 - To ease the casting problem with larger stern frames and also the transport problem, it may be cast in more than one piece and then welded together when erected in the shipyard.
[줄 1688] [100.0%] (26/26) ✅ 유지 - Fabricated stern frames are often produced by the shipyard itself, plates and bars being welded together to produce a form similar to that obtained by casting.
[줄 1689] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Forged stern frames are also produced by a specialist manufacturer and may also be made in more than one piece where the size is excessive or shape complicated.
[줄 1690] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - Sternpost sections are of a streamline form, in order to prevent eddies being formed behind the posts, which can lead to an increase in the hull resistance.
[줄 1691] [100.0%] (12/12) ✅ 유지 - Welded joints in cast steel sections will need careful preparation and preheat.
[줄 1692] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - Both the cast and fabricated sections are supported by horizontal webs.

[줄 1700] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - Rudders Many of the rudders that are found on present-day ships are semi-balanced, i.e they have a small proportion of their lateral area forward of the turning axis.
[줄 1701] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - Balanced rudders with a larger area forward of the axis and unbalanced rudders with the full area aft of the axis are also fitted.
[줄 1702] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - The object of balance is to achieve a reduction in torque, since the center of lateral pressure is brought nearer the turning axis.
[줄 1703] [100.0%] (36/36) ✅ 유지 - However, the fully balanced rudder will at low angles tend to drive the gear, which does not matter a great deal with power steering gears but is less satisfactory with any form of direct hand gear.
[줄 1704] [100.0%] (21/21) ✅ 유지 - Designs of rudders are various, and patent types are available, all of which claim increased efficiencies of one form or another.
[줄 1705] [84.0%] (21/25) ✅ 유지 - Two common forms of rudder are shown in Figure 21.4, each being associated with one of the stern frames shown in Figure 21.3.
[줄 1706] [100.0%] (27/27) ✅ 유지 - Rudder construction Modern rudders are of streamlined form except those on small vessels, and are fabricated from steel plate, the plate sides being stiffened by internal webs.
[줄 1707] [100.0%] (23/23) ✅ 유지 - Where the rudder is fully fabricated, one side plate is prepared and the vertical and horizontal stiffening webs are welded to this plate.
[줄 1708] [100.0%] (19/19) ✅ 유지 - The other plate, often called the 'closing plate', is then welded to the internal framing from the exterior only.
[줄 1709] [93.1%] (27/29) ✅ 유지 - This may be achieved by welding flat bars to the webs prior to fitting the closing plate, and then slot welding the plate as shown in Figure 21.4.
[줄 1710] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - Other rudders may have a cast frame and webs with welded side and closing plates, which are also shown in Figure 21.4.
[줄 1711] [100.0%] (45/45) ✅ 유지 - Minor features of the rudders are the provision of a drain hole at the bottom with a plug, and a lifting hole that can take the form of a short piece of tube welded through the rudder with doubling at the side and closing plates.
[줄 1712] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - To prevent internal corrosion the interior surfaces are suitably coated, and in some cases the rudder may be filled with an inert plastic foam.
[줄 1713] [85.0%] (17/20) ✅ 유지 - The rudder is tested when complete under a head of water 2.45 m above the top of the rudder.
[줄 1714] [88.0%] (22/25) ✅ 유지 - Rudder pintles Pintles on which the rudder turns in the gudgeons have a taper on the radius, and a bearing length that exceeds the diameter.
[줄 1715] [90.5%] (19/21) ✅ 유지 - Older ships may have a brass or bronze liner shrunk on the pintles, which turn in lignum vitae bearings fitted in

[줄 1720] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Rudder stock Rudder stock may be of cast or forged steel, and its meter is determined in accordance with the torque and any bending moment it is to withstand.
[줄 1721] [100.0%] (35/35) ✅ 유지 - At its lower end it is connected to the rudder by a horizontal or vertical bolted coupling, the bolts having a cross-sectional area that is adequate to withstand the torque applied to the stock.
[줄 1722] [93.3%] (14/15) ✅ 유지 - This coupling enables the rudder to be lifted from the pintles for inspection and service.
[줄 1723] [95.8%] (23/24) ✅ 유지 - Rudder bearing The weight of the rudder may be carried partly by the lower pintle and partly by a rudder bearer within the hull.
[줄 1724] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - In some rudder types, for example the spade type that is only supported within the hull, the full weight is borne by the bearer.
[줄 1725] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - A rudder bearer may incorporate the watertight gland fitted at the upper end of the rudder trunk, as shown in Figure 21.5.
[줄 1726] [93.9%] (31/33) ✅ 유지 - Most of the rudder's weight may come onto the bearer if excessive wear-down of the lower pintle occurs, and the bearers illustrated have cast iron cones that limit their wear-down.
[줄 1727] [100.0%] (41/41) ✅ 유지 - Rudder trunk Rudder stocks are carried in the rudder trunk, which as a rule is not made watertight at its lower end, but a watertight gland is fitted at the top of the trunk where the stock enters the intact hull.
[줄 1728] [100.0%] (34/34) ✅ 유지 - This trunk is kept reasonably short so that the stock has a minimum unsupported length, and may be constructed of plates welded in a box form with the transom floor forming its forward end.
[줄 1729] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - A small opening with watertight cover may be provided on one side of the trunk, which allows inspection of the stock from inside the hull in an emergency.
[줄 1730] [100.0%] (28/28) ✅ 유지 - Unless the main steering gear comprises two or more identical power units, every ship is to be provided with a main steering gear and an auxiliary steering gear.

[줄 1741] [91.7%] (22/24) ✅ 유지 - Sterntube A sterntube forms the after bearing for the propeller shaft, and incorporates the watertight gland where the shaft passes through the intact hull.
[줄 1742] [95.7%] (22/23) ✅ 유지 - Two forms of sterntube are in use, that most commonly fitted having water-lubricated bearings with the after end open to the sea.
[줄 1743] [100.0%] (16/16) ✅ 유지 - The other type is closed at both ends and has metal bearing surfaces lubricated by oil.
[줄 1744] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - In the former type the bearings were traditionally lignum vitae strips and the tail shaft was fitted with a brass liner.
[줄 1745] [90.0%] (9/10) ✅ 유지 - Today, composites are commonly used for water-lubricated sterntube bearings.
[줄 1746] [96.4%] (27/28) ✅ 유지 - The latter form of sterntube is preferred in many ships with machinery aft, where the short shaft is to be relatively stiff and only small deflections are tolerated.
[줄 1747] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - Where this patent oil-lubricated sterntube is fitted, glands are provided at both ends to retain the oil and prevent the ingress of water, white metal bearing surfaces being provided and the oil supplied from a reservoir.

[줄 1845] [91.9%] (34/37) ✅ 유지 - Mild steel As with dry cargo ships it is a requirement that Grade B, D, and E steels be used for the heavier plating of the main hull strength members where the greatest stresses arise in tankers.
[줄 1846] [83.3%] (10/12) ✅ 유지 - These requirements are the same as those indicated in Table 17.1.
[줄 1847] [82.5%] (33/40) ✅ 유지 - Grade E plates, which we have equated with the 'crack arrester strake' concept, will be seen to be required over the midship region in ships exceeding 250 meters in length and are also required as shown in Table 22.1.
[줄 1848] [100.0%] (29/29) ✅ 유지 - Higher tensile steel Higher tensile steels are often used for the deck and bottom regions of the larger tankers, Grades DH and EH being used for the heavier plating.
[줄 1849] [100.0%] (3/3) ✅ 유지 - As indicated in
[줄 1850] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - Chapter 5, the use of higher tensile steel leads to a reduction in the scantlings of these structural items with advantages both for the shipbuilder and owner.
[줄 1851] [100.0%] (38/38) ✅ 유지 - There is some concern that the thinner material may lead to problems if corrosion occurs, and that the thinner plate may also lead to additional fatigue problems due to excess movement of the structure under the forces encountered.
[줄 1852] [85.7%] (12/14) ✅ 유지 - The extent of this plating and section material is indicated in Figure 22.2.
[줄 1853] [97.5%] (39/40) ✅ 유지 - Construction in tank spaces Today's ocean-going crude oil tankers are generally large and in way of the tank spaces have a longitudinally framed double bottom supported by transverse floors and a longitudinally framed deck supported by deck transverses.
[줄 1854] [81.4%] (48/59) ✅ 유지 - The longitudinally Table 22.1 Use of Grade E steel in tankers Location Thickness Stringer plate, sheerstrake, rounded gunwale Greater than 15 mm Bilge strake, deck strake in way of longitudinal bulkhead Greater than 25 mm Main deck plating, bottom plating, keel, upper strake of longitudinal bulkhead Greater than 40 mm Stringer Transverse web Deck-transverse web CENTRE TANK
[줄 1855] [40.0%] (2/5) ❌ 제거 - Length B.P Beam mld.
[줄 1856] [65.9%] (27/41) ✅ 유지 - 315 m 58 m 30.4 m Plate bracket Inner bottom Intermediate stringer WING TANK Longitudinal bulkhead Inner hull Floor 3.5 m 3 m 'DH' 'EH' 'DH' 'DH' 'EH' 'EH' 'EH' 'DH' 'EH' Figure 22.2 Double-hull oil tanker.
[줄 1857] [100.0%] (22/22) ✅ 유지 - framed side shell, inner hull, and longitudinal bulkheads are all supported by transverse webs aligned with the transverse floors and deck transverses.
[줄 1858] [91.3%] (21/23) ✅ 유지 - Longitudinal framing Deck and bottom longitudinals have the greatest scantlings since they are stiffening the more highly stressed flanges of the hull girder.
[줄 1859] [92.6%] (25/27) ✅ 유지 - At the side shell the upper longitudinals have the least scantlings, and a uniform increase in size occurs down the side shell until the bilge is reached.
[줄 1860] [100.0%] (11/11) ✅ 유지 - The bilge longitudinal size then approaches that of the bottom shell.
[줄 1861] [95.2%] (20/21) ✅ 유지 - For products carriers the deck longitudinals may be fitted above the deck to provide a flush internal tank surface for cleaning.
[줄 1862] [100.0%] (24/24) ✅ 유지 - An important feature of the longitudinal framing is that continuity of strength is maintained, particularly at the bulkheads forming the ends of the tanks.
[줄 1863] [97.3%] (36/37) ✅ 유지 - This feature is increasingly important as the ship length is extended, the bottom and deck longitudinals being continuous through the bulkhead where the ship length is excessive, unless an alternative arrangement is permitted by the classification society.
[줄 1864] [91.7%] (11/12) ✅ 유지 - Higher tensile steel longitudinals are to be continuous irrespective of ship length.
[줄 1865] [90.0%] (18/20) ✅ 유지 - The longitudinals can be offset bulb plates that may be built up to give the required scantling on large ships.
[줄 1866] [95.5%] (21/22) ✅ 유지 - It is not, however, uncommon to find on many tankers specially fabricated tee longitudinals having a web and symmetrical flat plate flange.
[줄 1867] [93.8%] (15/16) ✅ 유지 - Floors and transverses To support the bottom and inner bottom longitudinals solid plate floors are fitted.
[줄 1868] [88.9%] (16/18) ✅ 유지 - Stiffened transverse plate webs support the side shell and inner shell longitudinals, deck longitudinals, and longitudinal bulkhead stiffening.
[줄 1869] [96.3%] (26/27) ✅ 유지 - In way of the center tank a bracketed deck transverse supports the deck longitudinals and large plate brackets are fitted between the longitudinal bulkheads and inner bottom.
[줄 1870] [96.8%] (30/31) ✅ 유지 - Transverses are as a rule built of a plate web and heavier flat face bar, the depth being adequate to allow sufficient material abreast the slots through which the longitudinals pass.
[줄 1871] [100.0%] (17/17) ✅ 유지 - Within the double-hull side space they form a solid web and are supported by horizontal stringers.
[줄 1872] [92.9%] (26/28) ✅ 유지 - In the wing tank space they support the deck longitudinals and fore and aft bulkhead longitudinals, and in turn are supported by a mid-height longitudinal plate stringer.
[줄 1873] [100.0%] (40/40) ✅ 유지 - Bottom and deck girders A center-line girder is required in the double-bottom space, which with the heavy keel plate constitutes the immediate structure through which docking loads are transmitted when the vessel is placed on the keel blocks.
[줄 1874] [57.1%] (4/7) ❌ 제거 - Deck No 4 B RIDGE A CCOMDT.
[줄 1875] [41.7%] (10/24) ❌ 제거 - DECKS QUARTER RAMP 3,2 DOWN UP 5,4 STERN RAMP 8 7 6 5 4 3 2 1 Figure 3.5 Car carrier.
